The amount of skid you will encounter depends on the specific implementation of a processor, and each vendor has its own solution to minimize it. Intel uses Precise Event Based Sampling (PEBS), which is rather good, but it still can, for example, blend the branch statistics across the comparison instruction and the following jump instruction. AMD employs its own Instruction Based Sampling (IBS), which tends to provide worse results in comparison.

Do note that the statistics presented by Tracy are a combination of two randomly sampled counters, so you should take them with a grain of salt. The random nature of sampling\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}63]\+ makes it entirely possible to count more branch misses than branch instructions or some other similar silliness. You should always cross-\/check this data with the count of sampled events to decide if you can reliably act upon the provided values.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}63]\+:\+ The hardware counters in practice can be triggered only once per million-\/or-\/so events happening.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md996}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Availability}{Availability}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md996}
Currently, the hardware performance counter readings are only available on Linux, which also includes the WSL2 layer on Windows\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}64]\+. Access to them is performed using the kernel-\/provided infrastructure, so what you get may depend on how your kernel was configured. This also means that the exact set of supported hardware is not known, as it depends on what has been implemented in Linux itself. At this point, the x86 hardware is fully supported (including features such as PEBS or IBS), and there\textquotesingle{}s PMU support on a selection of ARM designs. The performance counter data can be captured with no need for privilege elevation.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}64]\+:\+ You may need Windows 11 and the WSL preview from Microsoft Store for this to work.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_executableretrieval}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Executable code retrieval}{Executable code retrieval}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_executableretrieval}
Tracy will capture small chunks of the executable image during profiling to enable deep insight into program execution. The retrieved code can be subsequently disassembled to be inspected in detail. The profiler will perform this functionality only for functions no larger than 128 KB and only if symbol information is present.

The discovery of previously unseen executable code may result in reduced performance of real-\/time capture. This is especially true when the profiling session had just started. However, such behavior is expected and will go back to normal after several moments.

It would be best to be extra careful when working with non-\/public code, as parts of your program will be embedded in the captured trace. You can disable the collection of program code by compiling the profiled application with the {\ttfamily TRACY\+\_\+\+NO\+\_\+\+CODE\+\_\+\+TRANSFER} define. You can also strip the code from a saved trace using the {\ttfamily update} utility (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_dataremoval}{4.7.4}{3}4.\+7.\+4).

\begin{DoxyImportant}{Important}
{\bfseries{Important}} ~\newline
~\newline
 For proper program code retrieval, you can unload no module used by the application during the runtime. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_datalifetime}{3.1.1}{3}3.\+1.\+1 for an explanation. ~\newline
~\newline
 On Linux, Tracy will override the {\ttfamily dlclose} function call to prevent shared objects from being unloaded. Note that in a well-\/behaved program this shouldn\textquotesingle{}t have any effect, as calling {\ttfamily dlclose} does not guarantee that the shared object will be unloaded.
\end{DoxyImportant}
\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md997}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Vertical synchronization}{Vertical synchronization}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md997}
On Windows and Linux, Tracy will automatically capture hardware Vsync events, provided that the application has access to the kernel data (privilege elevation may be needed, see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_privilegeelevation}{3.18.1}{3}3.\+18.\+1). These events will be reported as "{}\`{}\+[x]\+ Vsync\`{}"{} frame sets, where {\ttfamily x} is the identifier of a specific monitor. Note that hardware vertical synchronization might not correspond to the one seen by your application due to desktop composition, command queue buffering, and so on. Also, in some instances, when there is nothing to update on the screen, the graphic driver may choose to stop issuing screen refresh. As a result, there may be periods where no vertical synchronization events are reported.

Use the {\ttfamily TRACY\+\_\+\+NO\+\_\+\+VSYNC\+\_\+\+CAPTURE} macro to disable capture of Vsync events.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_traceparameters}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Trace parameters}{Trace parameters}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_traceparameters}
Sometimes it is desired to change how the profiled application behaves during the profiling run. For example, you may want to enable or disable the capture of frame images without recompiling and restarting your program. To be able to do so you must register a callback function using the {\ttfamily Tracy\+Parameter\+Register(callback, data)} macro, where {\ttfamily callback} is a function conforming to the following signature:\+ \begin{DoxyVerb}void Callback(void* data, uint32_t idx, int32_t val)
\end{DoxyVerb}


The {\ttfamily data} parameter will have the same value as was specified in the macro. The {\ttfamily idx} argument is an user-\/defined parameter index and {\ttfamily val} is the value set in the profiler user interface (in the connection information popup, see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_connectionpopup}{4.4.2}{3}4.\+4.\+2).

To specify individual parameters, use the {\ttfamily Tracy\+Parameter\+Setup(idx, name, type, val)} macro. The {\ttfamily idx} value will be passed to the callback function for identification purposes (Tracy doesn\textquotesingle{}t care what it\textquotesingle{}s set to), {\ttfamily name} is the parameter label, displayed on the list of parameters, and {\ttfamily val} is the initial value. Finally, {\ttfamily type} determines how to interpret the {\ttfamily val} value, and can be selected from:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily Tracy\+Param\+Type\+Int} -- {\ttfamily val} is an integer value, with the profiler UI displaying a numerical entry field.
\item {\ttfamily Tracy\+Param\+Type\+Bool} -- {\ttfamily val} is a boolean value, with a checkbox in the user interface.
\item {\ttfamily Tracy\+Param\+Type\+Trigger} -- a {\itshape  Trigger} button is displayed, for cases when you just want some action to happen. Repeats the initial {\ttfamily val} value provided to the setup function.
\end{DoxyItemize}

\begin{DoxyImportant}{Important}
{\bfseries{Important}} ~\newline
~\newline
 Usage of trace parameters makes profiling runs dependent on user interaction with the profiler, and thus it\textquotesingle{}s not recommended to be employed if a consistent profiling environment is desired. Furthermore, interaction with the parameters is only possible in the graphical profiling application but not in the command line capture utility.
\end{DoxyImportant}
\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Circle Dot icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md999}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Source contents callback}{Source contents callback}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md999}
Tracy performs several data discovery attempts to show you the source file contents associated with the executed program, which is explained in more detail in chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sourceview}{5.17}{2}5.\+17. However, sometimes the source files cannot be accessed without your help. For example, you may want to profile a script that is loaded by the game and which only resides in an archive accessible only by your program. Accordingly, Tracy allows inserting your own custom step at the end of the source discovery chain, with the {\ttfamily Tracy\+Source\+Callback\+Register(callback, data)} macro, where {\ttfamily callback} is a function conforming to the following signature:\+ \begin{DoxyVerb}char* Callback(void* data, const char* filename, size_t& size)
\end{DoxyVerb}


The {\ttfamily data} parameter will have the same value as was specified in the macro. The {\ttfamily filename} parameter contains the file name of the queried source file. Finally, the {\ttfamily size} parameter is used only as an out-\/value and does not contain any functional data.

The return value must be {\ttfamily nullptr} if the input file name is not accessible to the client application. If the file can be accessed, then the data size must be stored in the {\ttfamily size} parameter, and the file contents must be returned in a buffer allocated with the {\ttfamily tracy::\+tracy\+\_\+malloc\+\_\+fast(size)} function. Buffer contents do not need to be null-\/terminated. If for some reason the already allocated buffer can no longer be used, it must be freed with the {\ttfamily tracy::\+tracy\+\_\+free\+\_\+fast(ptr)} function.

Transfer of source files larger than some unspecified, but reasonably large\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}65]\+ threshold won\textquotesingle{}t be performed.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}65]\+:\+ Let\textquotesingle{}s say around 256 \+KB sounds reasonable.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_connectionstatus}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Connection status}{Connection status}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_connectionstatus}
To determine if a connection is currently established between the client and the server, you may use the {\ttfamily Tracy\+Is\+Connected} macro, which returns a boolean value.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_capturing}{}\doxysection{\texorpdfstring{Capturing the data}{Capturing the data}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_capturing}
After the client application has been instrumented, you will want to connect to it using a server, available either as a headless capture-\/only utility or as a full-\/fledged graphical profiling interface.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1000}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Command line}{Command line}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1000}
You can capture a trace using a command line utility contained in the {\ttfamily capture} directory. To use it you may provide the following parameters:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily -\/o output.\+tracy} -- the file name of the resulting trace (required).
\item {\ttfamily -\/a address} -- specifies the IP address (or a domain name) of the client application (uses {\ttfamily localhost} if not provided).
\item {\ttfamily -\/p port} -- network port which should be used (optional).
\item {\ttfamily -\/f} -- force overwrite, if output file already exists.
\item {\ttfamily -\/s seconds} -- number of seconds to capture before automatically disconnecting (optional).
\item {\ttfamily -\/\doxylink{structm}{m} memlimit} -- sets memory limit for the trace. The connection will be terminated, if it is exceeded. Specified as a percentage of total system memory. Can be greater than 100\%, which will use swap. Disabled, if not set.
\end{DoxyItemize}

If no client is running at the given address, the server will wait until it can make a connection. During the capture, the utility will display the following information:\+ \begin{DoxyVerb}% ./tracy-capture -a 127.0.0.1 -o trace
Connecting to 127.0.0.1:8086...
Timer resolution: 3 ns
   1.33 Mbps / 40.4% = 3.29 Mbps | Net: 64.42 MB | Mem: 283.03 MB | Time: 10.6 s
\end{DoxyVerb}


The {\itshape timer resolution} parameter shows the calibration results of timers used by the client. The following line is a status bar, which displays:\+ network connection speed, connection compression ratio, and the resulting uncompressed data rate; the total amount of data transferred over the network; memory usage of the capture utility; time extent of the captured data.

You can disconnect from the client and save the captured trace by pressing Ctrl + C. If you prefer to disconnect after a fixed time, use the {\ttfamily -\/s seconds} parameter.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1001}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Multi-\/client capture daemon}{Multi-\/client capture daemon}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1001}
If you want to capture profiling data from multiple clients simultaneously, you can use the {\ttfamily tracy-\/capture-\/daemon} utility. This tool listens for UDP broadcast messages from Tracy clients on the network, automatically discovers available clients, and captures each one to a separate file.

The daemon accepts the following parameters:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily -\/o, -\/-\/output \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}dir\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} -- output directory for captured traces (required, created if it doesn\textquotesingle{}t exist).
\item {\ttfamily -\/p, -\/-\/port \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}port\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} -- UDP listen port (default:\+ 8086).
\item {\ttfamily -\/\doxylink{structm}{m}, -\/-\/memory \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}limit\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} -- sets memory limit per client. Specified as a percentage of total system memory.
\item {\ttfamily -\/-\/filter-\/name \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}pattern\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} -- only capture clients whose program name matches the pattern.
\item {\ttfamily -\/-\/filter-\/port \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}port\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} -- only capture clients with the specified data port.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Usage example:\+


\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\{sh\ language="{}sh"{}\}\ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\$\ tracy-\/capture-\/daemon\ -\/o\ ./traces}
\DoxyCodeLine{[3\ clients]\ Listening\ on\ 0.0.0.0:8086...\ Press\ Ctrl+C\ to\ stop}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ [1]\ myapp\ @\ 192.168.1.10:9086\ \ \ \ 45.2\ Mbps\ |\ 234\ MB\ |\ 12.3\ s}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ [2]\ server\ @\ 192.168.1.11:9086\ \ \ 38.7\ Mbps\ |\ 189\ MB\ |\ 11.8\ s}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ [3]\ worker\ @\ 192.168.1.12:9086\ \ \ 22.1\ Mbps\ |\ 145\ MB\ |\ 10.2\ s}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{Total:\ 106.0\ Mbps\ |\ 568\ MB\ |\ Mem:\ 321\ MB}

\end{DoxyCode}


Each client is captured to a separate file in the output directory, named according to the pattern {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}program\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}\+\_\+\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}ip\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}\+\_\+\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}port\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}.tracy}. If a client reconnects, a sequence number is appended (e.\+g., {\ttfamily myapp\+\_\+192.\+168.\+1.\+10\+\_\+9086\+\_\+1.\+tracy}).

Press Ctrl + C to stop discovery and gracefully shut down all active captures. Each capture thread will finish writing its trace file before the daemon exits.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_mergingtraces}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Merging trace files}{Merging trace files}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_mergingtraces}
When you have captured multiple traces using the capture daemon, you can combine them into a single trace file using the {\ttfamily tracy-\/merge} utility in the {\ttfamily merge} directory. This is useful for analyzing a multi-\/process application in a single view.

The tool accepts the following parameters:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily -\/o, -\/-\/output \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}file\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} -- \doxylink{struct_output}{Output} file path (required)
\item {\ttfamily -\/f, -\/-\/force} -- Overwrite output file if it exists
\item {\ttfamily -\/h, -\/-\/help} -- Display a help message
\end{DoxyItemize}

Usage example:\+


\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\{sh\ language="{}sh"{}\}\ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\$\ tracy-\/merge\ -\/o\ merged.tracy\ trace1.tracy\ trace2.tracy\ trace3.tracy}

\end{DoxyCode}


To prevent thread ID collisions between traces from different processes, thread names are prefixed with the process name. If the same process and thread name appear in multiple traces, the PID is included for disambiguation (e.\+g., {\ttfamily myapp\+[12345]\+/\+\+Main\+Thread}). See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_importingdata}{8}{1}8 for details on how PID+\+TID pairs are handled.

\begin{DoxyAttention}{Attention}
{\bfseries{Limitations}} ~\newline
~\newline

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Time is {\bfseries{not synchronized}} between input traces. The tool is designed for merging traces captured simultaneously (e.\+g., from a multi-\/process application). Merging traces from different capture sessions or different machines will result in misaligned timestamps. ~\newline
~\newline

\item The tool uses the Import API, which only preserves zones, messages, and plots. The following data is {\bfseries{lost}} during merge:\+ ~\newline
~\newline

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item GPU zones ~\newline
~\newline

\item Memory allocation events ~\newline
~\newline

\item Callstacks ~\newline
~\newline

\item Lock events ~\newline
~\newline

\item Context switches ~\newline
~\newline

\item Frame images ~\newline
~\newline

\end{DoxyItemize}
\item Plots always use the {\ttfamily Number} format, regardless of the original format specification.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyAttention}
\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_interactiveprofiling}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Interactive profiling}{Interactive profiling}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_interactiveprofiling}
If you want to look at the profile data in real-\/time (or load a saved trace file), you can use the data analysis utility {\ttfamily tracy-\/profiler} contained in the {\ttfamily profiler} directory. After starting the application, you will be greeted with a welcome dialog (figure 88), presenting a bunch of useful links ( {\itshape User manual},  {\itshape Web},  {\itshape Join chat} and  {\itshape Sponsor}). The  {\itshape Web} button opens a drop-\/down list with links to the profiler\textquotesingle{}s {\itshape  Home page} and a bunch of {\itshape  Feature videos}.

The {\itshape  Wrench} button opens the about dialog, which also contains a number of global settings you may want to tweak (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_aboutwindow}{4.4.1}{3}4.\+4.\+1).

The client {\itshape address entry} field and the  {\itshape Connect} button are used to connect to a running client\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}66]\+. You can use the connection history button  to display a list of commonly used targets, from which you can quickly select an address. You can remove entries from this list by hovering the  mouse cursor over an entry and pressing the Delete button on the keyboard.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}66]\+:\+ Note that a custom port may be provided here, for example by entering "{}127.\+0.\+0.\+1:\+1234"{}.

If you want to open a trace that you have stored on the disk, you can do so by pressing the  {\itshape Open saved trace} button.

The {\itshape discovered clients} list is only displayed if clients are broadcasting their presence on the local network\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}67]\+. Each entry shows the client\textquotesingle{}s address\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}68]\+ (and port, if different from the default one), how long the client has been running, and the name of the profiled application. Clicking on an entry will connect to the client. Incompatible clients are grayed out and can\textquotesingle{}t be connected to, but Tracy will suggest a compatible version, if able. Clicking on the {\itshape  Filter} toggle button will display client filtering input fields, allowing removal of the displayed entries according to their address, port number, or program name. If filters are active, a yellow  warning icon will be displayed.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}67]\+:\+ Only on IPv4 network and only within the broadcast domain.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}68]\+:\+ Either as an IP address or as a hostname, if able to resolve.

$<$figure id="{}welcomedialog"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Welcome dialog.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

Both connecting to a client and opening a saved trace will present you with the main profiler view, which you can use to analyze the data (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_analyzingdata}{5}{1}5).

Once connected to a client Ctrl + Shift + Alt + R can be used to quickly discard any captured data and reconnect to a client at the same address.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Book icon  -\/ Earth Americas icon  -\/ Comments icon  -\/ Heart icon  -\/ House Chimney icon  -\/ Video icon  -\/ Wrench icon  -\/ Wifi icon  -\/ Caret Down icon  -\/ Arrow Pointer icon  -\/ Folder Open icon  -\/ Filter icon  -\/ Triangle Exclamation icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_aboutwindow}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{About window}{About window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_aboutwindow}
The About window displays the profiler version and the Git SHA identifier of the build, as well as some additional information.

You can also adjust some settings that affect global profiler behavior in this window. These settings are accessible by expanding the {\itshape  Global settings} node. The following options are available:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Threaded rendering} -- This controls whether the profiler UI uses multithreaded rendering. Since the profiler needs to quickly navigate large amounts of data, it spends a lot of time waiting for memory accesses to be resolved. Multithreading enables multiple simultaneous memory reads, which significantly reduces the impact of memory access latency. However, this may result in higher CPU usage, which could interfere with the application you are profiling.
\item {\itshape Reduce render rate when focus is lost} -- This throttles the profiler window refresh rate to 20 FPS when the window does not have focus.
\item {\itshape Target FPS} -- Sets the default {\itshape target FPS} value for the {\itshape Frame time graph}. See sections \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frametimegraph}{5.2.2}{3}5.\+2.\+2
\end{DoxyItemize}and \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4 for more information. Not related to the profiler window refresh rate.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Zone colors} -- Sets the default zone coloring preset used in new traces. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4
\end{DoxyItemize}for more information.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Zone name shortening} -- Sets the default zone name shortening behavior used in new traces. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4
\end{DoxyItemize}for more information.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Scroll multipliers} -- Allows you to fine-\/tune the sensitivity of the horizontal and vertical scroll in the timeline. The default values (1.\+0) are an attempt at the best possible settings, but differences in hardware manufacturers, platform implementations, and user expectations may require adjustments.
\item {\itshape Memory limit} -- When enabled, profiler will stop recording data when memory usage exceeds the specified percentage of the total system memory. This mechanism does not measure the current system memory usage or limits. The upper value is not capped, as you may use swap. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memoryusage}{4.6}{2}4.\+6
\end{DoxyItemize}for more information.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Enable achievements} -- Enables achievements system, accessed through the  icon in the bottom right corner of the profiler window. It is essentially a gamified tutorial system designed to teach new users how to use the profiler.
\item {\itshape Save UI scale} -- Determines whether the UI scale set by the user should be saved between sessions. This setting is not related to DPI scaling.
\item {\itshape Enable Tracy Assist} -- Controls whether the automated assistant features (based on large language models) are available through the Profiler UI. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_tracyassist}{6}{1}6
\end{DoxyItemize}for more details.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Toolbox icon  -\/ Star icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_connectionpopup}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Connection information pop-\/up}{Connection information pop-\/up}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_connectionpopup}
If this is a real-\/time capture, you will also have access to the connection information pop-\/up (figure 99) through the {\itshape  Connection} button, with the capture status similar to the one displayed by the command-\/line utility. This dialog also shows the connection speed graphed over time and the profiled application\textquotesingle{}s current frames per second and frame time measurements. The {\itshape Query backlog} consists of two numbers. The first represents the number of queries that were held back due to the bandwidth volume overwhelming the available network send buffer. The second one shows how many queries are in-\/flight, meaning requests sent to the client but not yet answered. While these numbers drain down to zero, the performance of real time profiling may be temporarily compromised. The circle displayed next to the bandwidth graph signals the connection status. If it\textquotesingle{}s red, the connection is active. If it\textquotesingle{}s gray, the client has disconnected.

You can use the  {\itshape Save trace} button to save the current profile data to a file\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}69]\+. The available compression modes are discussed in sections \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_archival}{4.7.1}{3}4.\+7.\+1 and \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_fidict}{4.7.3}{3}4.\+7.\+3. Use the  {\itshape Stop} button to disconnect from the client\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}70]\+. The  {\itshape Discard} button is used to discard current trace.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}69]\+:\+ You should take this literally. If a live capture is in progress and a save is performed, some data may be missing from the capture and won\textquotesingle{}t be saved.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}70]\+:\+ While requesting disconnect stops retrieval of any new events, the profiler will wait for any data that is still pending for the current set of events.

$<$figure id="{}connectioninfo"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Connection information pop-\/up.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

If frame image capture has been implemented (chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frameimages}{3.3.3}{3}3.\+3.\+3), a thumbnail of the last received frame image will be provided for reference.

Suppose the profiled application opted to provide trace parameters (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_traceparameters}{3.19}{2}3.\+19) and the connection is still active. In that case, this pop-\/up will also contain a {\itshape Trace parameters} section, listing all the provided options. A callback function will be executed on the client when you change any value here.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Wifi icon  -\/ Floppy Disk icon  -\/ Plug icon  -\/ Triangle Exclamation icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1005}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Automatic loading or connecting}{Automatic loading or connecting}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1005}
You can pass the trace file name as an argument to the profiler application to open the capture, skipping the welcome dialog. You can also use the {\ttfamily -\/a address} argument to connect to the given address automatically. Finally, to specify the network port, pass the {\ttfamily -\/p port} parameter. The profiler will use it for client connections (overridable in the UI) and for listening to client discovery broadcasts.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1006}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Connection speed}{Connection speed}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1006}
Tracy network bandwidth requirements depend on the amount of data collection the profiled application performs. You may expect anything between 1 \+Mbps and 100 \+Mbps data transfer rate in typical use case scenarios.

The maximum attainable connection speed is determined by the ability of the client to provide data and the ability of the server to process the received data. In an extreme conditions test performed on an i7 8700K, the maximum transfer rate peaked at 950 \+Mbps. In each second, the profiler could process 27 million zones and consume 1 \+GB of RAM.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memoryusage}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Memory usage}{Memory usage}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memoryusage}
The captured data is stored in RAM and only written to the disk when the capture finishes. This can result in memory exhaustion when you capture massive amounts of profile data or even in typical usage situations when the capture is performed over a long time. Therefore, the recommended usage pattern is to perform moderate instrumentation of the client code and limit capture time to the strict necessity.

In some cases, it may be helpful to perform an {\itshape on-\/demand} capture, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_ondemand}{2.1.5}{3}2.\+1.\+5. In such a case, you will be able to profile only the exciting topic (e.\+g., behavior during loading of a level in a game), ignoring all the unneeded data.

If you genuinely need to capture large traces, you have two options. Either buy more RAM or use a large swap file on a fast disk drive\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}71]\+.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}71]\+:\+ The operating system can manage memory paging much better than Tracy would be ever able to.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1007}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Trace versioning}{Trace versioning}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1007}
Each new release of Tracy changes the internal format of trace files. While there is a backward compatibility layer, allowing loading traces created by previous versions of Tracy in new releases, it won\textquotesingle{}t be there forever. You are thus advised to upgrade your traces using the utility contained in the {\ttfamily update} directory.

To use it, you will need to provide the input file and the output file. The program will print a short summary when it finishes, with information about trace file versions, their respective sizes and the output trace file compression ratio:\+ \begin{DoxyVerb}% ./tracy-update old.tracy new.tracy
old.tracy (0.3.0) {916.4 MB} -> new.tracy (0.4.0) {349.4 MB, 31.53%}  9.7 s, 38.13% change
\end{DoxyVerb}


The new file contains the same data as the old one but with an updated internal representation. Note that the whole trace needs to be loaded to memory to perform an upgrade.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_archival}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Archival mode}{Archival mode}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_archival}
The {\ttfamily update} utility supports optional higher levels of data compression, which reduce disk size of traces at the cost of increased compression times. The output files have a reasonable size and are quick to save and load with the default settings. A list of available compression modes and their respective results is available in table 88 and figures 1010, 1212 and 1313. The following command-\/line options control compression mode selection:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily -\/4} -- selects LZ4 algorithm.
\item {\ttfamily -\/h} -- enables LZ4 HC compression.
\item {\ttfamily -\/e} -- uses LZ4 extreme compression.
\item {\ttfamily -\/z level} -- selects Zstandard algorithm, with a specified compression level.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyTable}{5}{}{}{1}

$<$figure id="{}savetime"{}$>$ $<$figure id="{}savesize"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}\+H"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Logarithmic plot of trace compression times for different compression modes (see table \href{\#compressiontimes}{\texttt{8}}).$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$ $<$figcaption$>$Logarithmic plot of trace compression times for different compression modes (see table \href{\#compressiontimes}{\texttt{8}}).$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

$<$figure id="{}loadtime"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Plot of trace load times for different compression modes (see table \href{\#compressiontimes}{\texttt{8}}).$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

Trace files created using the {\itshape lz4}, {\itshape lz4 hc} and {\itshape lz4 extreme} modes are optimized for fast decompression and can be further compressed using file compression utilities. For example, using 7-\/zip results in archives of the following sizes:\+ 77.\+2 MB, 54.\+3 MB, 52.\+4 MB.

For archival purposes, it is, however, much better to use the {\itshape zstd} compression modes, which are faster, compress trace files more tightly, and are directly loadable by the profiler, without the intermediate decompression step.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1008}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Compression streams}{Compression streams}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1008}
Saving and loading trace data can be parallelized using the {\ttfamily -\/j streams} parameter. Each compression stream runs on its own thread, and it makes little sense to use more streams than you have CPU cores. Note that the number of streams set at save time will also be used at load time, which may affect load performance if you are viewing the trace on a less powerful machine.

Going overboard with the number of streams is not recommended, especially with the fast compression modes where it will be difficult to keep each stream busy. Also, complex compression codecs (e.\+g. zstd at level 22) have significantly worse compression rates when the work is divided. This is a fairly nuanced topic, and you are encouraged to do your own measurements, but for a rough guideline on the behavior, you can refer to tables 99 and 1010.


\begin{DoxyTable}{5}{}{}{1}
\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}&\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}{\bfseries{4}}  &\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}{\bfseries{8}}  &\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}{\bfseries{16}}  &\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}{\bfseries{32}}  \\
\SetCell{c}lz4  &\SetCell{c}100.\+30\%  &\SetCell{c}100.\+30\%  &\SetCell{c}100.\+61\%  &\SetCell{c}102.\+73\%  \\
\SetCell{c}lz4 hc  &\SetCell{c}100.\+80\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+20\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+61\%  &\SetCell{c}102.\+41\%  \\
\SetCell{c}lz4 ext  &\SetCell{c}100.\+40\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+21\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+62\%  &\SetCell{c}102.\+02\%  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 1  &\SetCell{c}100.\+90\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+36\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+81\%  &\SetCell{c}102.\+26\%  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 3  &\SetCell{c}100.\+51\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+02\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+53\%  &\SetCell{c}102.\+04\%  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 6  &\SetCell{c}100.\+55\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+10\%  &\SetCell{c}101.\+65\%  &\SetCell{c}102.\+75\%  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 9  &\SetCell{c}101.\+27\%  &\SetCell{c}103.\+16\%  &\SetCell{c}105.\+06\%  &\SetCell{c}108.\+23\%  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 18  &\SetCell{c}103.\+08\%  &\SetCell{c}106.\+15\%  &\SetCell{c}109.\+23\%  &\SetCell{c}115.\+38\%  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 22  &\SetCell{c}107.\+08\%  &\SetCell{c}113.\+27\%  &\SetCell{c}122.\+12\%  &\SetCell{c}130.\+97\%  \\
\end{DoxyTable}


{\itshape The increase in file size for different compression modes, as compared to a single stream.}

\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}&\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}{\bfseries{4}}  &\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}{\bfseries{8}}  &\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}{\bfseries{16}}  &\SetCell{c,bg=\tableheadbgcolor,font=\bfseries}{\bfseries{32}}  \\
\SetCell{c}lz4  &\SetCell{c}2.\+04  &\SetCell{c}2.\+52  &\SetCell{c}2.\+11  &\SetCell{c}3.\+24  \\
\SetCell{c}lz4 hc  &\SetCell{c}3.\+56  &\SetCell{c}6.\+73  &\SetCell{c}9.\+49  &\SetCell{c}15.\+26  \\
\SetCell{c}lz4 ext  &\SetCell{c}3.\+38  &\SetCell{c}6.\+53  &\SetCell{c}9.\+57  &\SetCell{c}17.\+03  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 1  &\SetCell{c}2.\+24  &\SetCell{c}3.\+68  &\SetCell{c}3.\+40  &\SetCell{c}3.\+37  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 3  &\SetCell{c}3.\+23  &\SetCell{c}4.\+13  &\SetCell{c}4.\+07  &\SetCell{c}4.\+50  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 6  &\SetCell{c}3.\+52  &\SetCell{c}6.\+00  &\SetCell{c}6.\+53  &\SetCell{c}6.\+95  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 9  &\SetCell{c}3.\+10  &\SetCell{c}4.\+26  &\SetCell{c}5.\+12  &\SetCell{c}5.\+40  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 18  &\SetCell{c}3.\+22  &\SetCell{c}5.\+41  &\SetCell{c}8.\+49  &\SetCell{c}14.\+51  \\
\SetCell{c}zstd 22  &\SetCell{c}3.\+99  &\SetCell{c}7.\+47  &\SetCell{c}11.\+10  &\SetCell{c}18.\+20  \\
\end{DoxyTable}


{\itshape The speedup ({\itshape x} times faster) in saving time for different modes of compression, as compared to a single stream.}\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_fidict}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Frame images dictionary}{Frame images dictionary}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_fidict}
Frame images have to be compressed individually so that there are no delays during random access to the contents of any image. Unfortunately, because of this, there is no reuse of compression state between similar (or even identical) images, which leads to increased memory consumption. The profiler can partially remedy this by enabling the calculation of an optional frame images dictionary with the {\ttfamily -\/d} command line parameter.

Saving a trace with frame images dictionary-\/enabled will need some extra time, depending on the amount of image data you have captured. Loading such a trace will also be slower, but not by much. How much RAM the dictionary will save depends on the similarity of frame images. Be aware that post-\/processing effects such as artificial film grain have a subtle impact on image contents, which is significant in this case.

The dictionary cannot be used when you are capturing a trace.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_dataremoval}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Data removal}{Data removal}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_dataremoval}
In some cases you may want to share just a portion of the trace file, omitting sensitive data such as source file cache, or machine code of the symbols. This can be achieved using the {\ttfamily -\/s flags} command line option. To select what kind of data is to be stripped, you need to provide a list of flags selected from the following:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily l} -- locks.
\item {\ttfamily \doxylink{structm}{m}} -- messages.
\item {\ttfamily p} -- plots.
\item {\ttfamily M} -- memory.
\item {\ttfamily i} -- frame images.
\item {\ttfamily c} -- context switches.
\item {\ttfamily s} -- sampling data.
\item {\ttfamily C} -- symbol code.
\item {\ttfamily S} -- source file cache.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Flags can be concatenated. For example specifying {\ttfamily -\/s CSi} will remove symbol code, source file cache, and frame images in the destination trace file.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1009}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Source file cache scan}{Source file cache scan}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1009}
Sometimes access to source files may not be possible during the capture. This may be due to capturing the trace on a machine without the source files on disk, use of paths relative to the build directory, clash of file location schemas (e.\+g., on Windows, you can have native paths, like {\ttfamily C:\+\textbackslash{}directory\textbackslash{}file} and WSL paths, like {\ttfamily /\+mnt/\+c/\+directory/\+file}, pointing to the same file), and so on.

You may force a recheck of the source file availability during the update process with the {\ttfamily -\/c} command line parameter. All the source files missing from the cache will be then scanned again and added to the cache if they do pass the validity checks (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sourceview}{5.17}{2}5.\+17).\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_instrumentationfailures}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Instrumentation failures}{Instrumentation failures}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_instrumentationfailures}
In some cases, your program may be incorrectly instrumented. For example, you could have unbalanced zone begin and end events or report a memory-\/free event without first reporting a memory allocation event. When Tracy detects such misbehavior, it immediately terminates the connection with the client and displays an error message.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_analyzingdata}{}\doxysection{\texorpdfstring{Analyzing captured data}{Analyzing captured data}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_analyzingdata}
You have instrumented your application, and you have captured a profiling trace. Now you want to look at the collected data. You can do this in the application contained in the {\ttfamily profiler} directory.

The workflow is identical, whether you are viewing a previously saved trace or if you\textquotesingle{}re performing a live capture, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_interactiveprofiling}{4.4}{2}4.\+4.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1010}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Time display}{Time display}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1010}
In most cases Tracy will display an approximation of time value, depending on how big it is. For example, a short time range will be displayed as 123 ns, and some longer ones will be shortened to 123.\+45 μs, 123.\+45 ms, 12.\+34 s, 1:\+23.\+4, 12:\+34:\+56, or even 1d12:\+34:\+56 to indicate more than a day has passed.

While such a presentation makes time values easy to read, it is not always appropriate. For example, you may have multiple events happen at a time approximated to 1:\+23.\+4, giving you the precision of only 1/\+10 of a second. And there\textquotesingle{}s certainly a lot that can happen in 100 ms.

An alternative time display is used in appropriate places to solve this problem. It combines a day--hour--minute--second value with full nanosecond resolution, resulting in values such as 1:\+23 456,789,012 ns.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1011}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Main profiler window}{Main profiler window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1011}
The main profiler window is split into three sections, as seen in figure 1414:\+ the control menu, the frame time graph, and the timeline display.

$<$figure id="{}mainwindow"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Main profiler window. Note that this manual has split the top line of buttons into two rows.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_controlmenu}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Control menu}{Control menu}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_controlmenu}
The control menu (top row of buttons) provides access to various profiler features. The buttons perform the following actions:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Connection} -- Opens the connection information popup (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_connectionpopup}{4.4.2}{3}4.\+4.\+2
\end{DoxyItemize}). Only available when live capture is in progress.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Close} -- This button unloads the current profiling trace and returns to the welcome menu, where another trace can be loaded. In live captures it is replaced by {\itshape  Pause}, {\itshape  Resume} and {\itshape  Stopped} buttons.
\item {\itshape  Pause} -- While a live capture is in progress, the profiler will display recent events, as either the last three fully captured frames, or a certain time range. You can use this to see the current behavior of the program. The pause button\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}72]\+ will stop the automatic updates of the timeline view (the capture will still be progressing).
\item {\itshape  Resume} -- This button allows to resume following the most recent events in a live capture. You will have selection of one of the following options:\+ {\itshape  Newest three frames}, or {\itshape  Use current zoom level}.
\item {\itshape  Stopped} -- Inactive button used to indicate that the client application was terminated.
\item {\itshape  Options} -- Toggles the settings menu (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Messages} -- Toggles the message log window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_messages}{5.5}{2}5.\+5
\end{DoxyItemize}), which displays custom messages sent by the client, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_messagelog}{3.8}{2}3.\+8.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Find} -- This buttons toggles the find zone window, which allows inspection of zone behavior statistics (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Statistics} -- Toggles the statistics window, which displays zones sorted by their total time cost (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_statistics}{5.6}{2}5.\+6
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Flame} -- Enables the flame graph window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_flamegraph}{5.9}{2}5.\+9
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Memory} -- Various memory profiling options may be accessed here (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memorywindow}{5.10}{2}5.\+10
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Compare} -- Toggles the trace compare window, which allows you to see the performance difference between two profiling runs (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_compare}{5.8}{2}5.\+8
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Info} -- Show general information about the trace (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_traceinfo}{5.13}{2}5.\+13
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Tools} -- Allows access to optional data collected during capture. Some choices might be unavailable.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Playback} -- If frame images were captured (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frameimages}{3.3.3}{3}3.\+3.\+3
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyItemize}), you will have option to open frame image playback window, described in chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_playback}{5.20}{2}5.\+20.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  CPU data} -- If context switch data was captured (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_contextswitches}{3.18.3}{3}3.\+18.\+3
\end{DoxyItemize}), this button will allow inspecting what was the processor load during the capture, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_cpudata}{5.21}{2}5.\+21.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Annotations} -- If annotations have been made (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_annotatingtrace}{5.3.1}{3}5.\+3.\+1
\end{DoxyItemize}), you can open a list of all annotations, described in chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_annotationlist}{5.23}{2}5.\+23.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Limits} -- Displays time range limits window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timeranges}{5.3}{2}5.\+3
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Wait stacks} -- If sampling was performed, an option to display wait stacks may be available. See chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_waitstacks}{3.18.5.1}{4}3.\+18.\+5.\+1
\end{DoxyItemize}for more details.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Frame statistics} -- Display frame statistics window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_framestatistics}{5.14}{2}5.\+14
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  User manual} -- Opens the user manual for quick reference. Note that the version of the user manual available directly in the profiler is an inferior quality version compared to the proper PDF.
\item {\itshape  Display scale} -- Enables run-\/time resizing of the displayed content. This may be useful in environments with potentially reduced visibility, e.\+g. during a presentation. Note that this setting is independent to the UI scaling coming from the system DPI settings. The scale will be preserved across multiple profiler sessions if the {\itshape Save UI scale} option is selected in global settings.
\item {\itshape  Tracy Assist} -- Shows the automated assistant chat window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_tracyassist}{6}{1}6
\end{DoxyItemize}). Only available if enabled in global settings (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_aboutwindow}{4.4.1}{3}4.\+4.\+1).

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}72]\+:\+ Or perform any action on the timeline view, apart from changing the zoom level.

The frame information block\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}73]\+ consists of four elements:\+ the current frame set name along with the number of captured frames (click on it with the left mouse button to go to a specified frame), the two navigational buttons  and , which allow you to focus the timeline view on the previous or next frame, and the frame set selection button , which is used to switch to another frame set\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}74]\+. For more information about marking frames, see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_markingframes}{3.3}{2}3.\+3.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}73]\+:\+ Visible only if frame instrumentation was included in the capture.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}74]\+:\+ See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_framesets}{5.2.3.2}{4}5.\+2.\+3.\+2 for another way to change the active frame set.

The following three items show the {\itshape  view time range}, the {\itshape  time span} of the whole capture (clicking on it with the middle mouse button will set the view range to the entire capture), and the {\itshape  memory usage} of the profiler.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Wifi icon  -\/ Power Off icon  -\/ Pause icon  -\/ Play icon  -\/ Square icon  -\/ Magnifying Glass Plus icon  -\/ Ruler Horizontal icon  -\/ Gear icon  -\/ Comment icon  -\/ Magnifying Glass icon  -\/ Arrow Up Wide Short icon  -\/ Fire Flame Curved icon  -\/ Memory icon  -\/ Scale Balanced icon  -\/ Fingerprint icon  -\/ Screwdriver Wrench icon  -\/ Sliders icon  -\/ Note Sticky icon  -\/ Ruler icon  -\/ Hourglass Half icon  -\/ Images icon  -\/ Book icon  -\/ Robot icon  -\/ Caret Left icon  -\/ Caret Right icon  -\/ Caret Down icon  -\/ Eye icon  -\/ Database icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1013}{}\doxysubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Notification area}{Notification area}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1013}
The notification area displays informational notices, for example, how long it took to load a trace from the disk. The three pulsing dots indicator shows that some background tasks are being performed that may need to be completed before full capabilities of the profiler are available. If a crash was captured during profiling (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_crashhandling}{2.5}{2}2.\+5), a {\itshape  crash} icon will be displayed. You can click this icon to see the crash call stack. The red  icon indicates that queries are currently being backlogged, while the same yellow icon indicates that some queries are currently in-\/flight (see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_connectionpopup}{4.4.2}{3}4.\+4.\+2 for more information).

If the drawing of timeline elements was disabled in the options menu (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4), the profiler will use the following orange icons to remind you about that fact. Click on the icons to enable drawing of the selected elements. Note that collapsed labels (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneslocksplots}{5.2.3.4}{4}5.\+2.\+3.\+4) are not taken into account here.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item  -- Display of empty labels is enabled.
\item  -- Context switches are hidden.
\item  -- CPU data is hidden.
\item  -- GPU zones are hidden.
\item  -- CPU zones are hidden.
\item  -- Locks are hidden.
\item  -- Plots are hidden.
\item  -- Ghost zones are not displayed.
\item  -- At least one timeline item (e.\+g. a single thread, a single plot, a single lock, etc.) is hidden.
\end{DoxyItemize}

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Skull icon  -\/ Satellite Dish icon  -\/ Expand icon  -\/ Person Hiking icon  -\/ Sliders icon  -\/ Eye icon  -\/ Microchip icon  -\/ Lock icon  -\/ Signature icon  -\/ Ghost icon  -\/ Eye Low Vision icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frametimegraph}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Frame time graph}{Frame time graph}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frametimegraph}
The graph of the currently selected frame set (figure 1515) provides an outlook on the time spent in each frame, allowing you to see where the problematic frames are and to navigate to them quickly.

$<$figure id="{}frametime"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Frame time graph.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

Each bar displayed on the graph represents a unique frame in the current frame set\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}75]\+. The progress of time is in the right direction. The bar height indicates the time spent in the frame, complemented by the color information, which depends on the target FPS value. You can set the desired FPS in the options menu (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4).

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}75]\+:\+ Unless the view is zoomed out and multiple frames are merged into one column.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If the bar is {\itshape blue}, then the frame met the {\itshape best} time of twice the target FPS (represented by the green target line).
\item If the bar is {\itshape green}, then the frame met the {\itshape good} time of target FPS (represented by the yellow line).
\item If the bar is {\itshape yellow}, then the frame met the {\itshape bad} time of half the FPS (represented by the red target line).
\item If the bar is {\itshape red}, then the frame didn\textquotesingle{}t meet any time limits.
\end{DoxyItemize}

The frames visible on the timeline are marked with a violet box drawn over them.

When a zone is displayed in the find zone window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7), the coloring of frames may be changed, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frametimefindzone}{5.7.2}{3}5.\+7.\+2.

Moving the  mouse cursor over the frames displayed on the graph will display a tooltip with information about frame number, frame time, frame image (if available, see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frameimages}{3.3.3}{3}3.\+3.\+3), etc. Such tooltips are common for many UI elements in the profiler and won\textquotesingle{}t be mentioned later in the manual.

You may focus the timeline view on the frames by clicking or dragging the left mouse button on the graph. The graph may be scrolled left and right by dragging the right mouse button over the graph. Finally, you may zoom the view in and out by using the mouse wheel. If the view is zoomed out, so that multiple frames are merged into one column, the profiler will use the highest frame time to represent the given column.

Clicking the left mouse button on the graph while the Ctrl key is pressed will open the frame image playback window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_playback}{5.20}{2}5.\+20) and set the playback to the selected frame. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frameimages}{3.3.3}{3}3.\+3.\+3 for more information about frame images.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1016}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Timeline view}{Timeline view}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1016}
The timeline is the most crucial element of the profiler UI. All the captured data is displayed there, laid out on the horizontal axis, according to time flow. Where there was no profiling performed, the timeline is dimmed out. The view is split into four parts:\+ time scale, frame sets, sections, and the combined zones, locks, and plots display.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collapseditems}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Collapsed items}{Collapsed items}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collapseditems}
Due to extreme differences in time scales, you will almost constantly see events too small to be displayed on the screen. Such events have preset minimum size (so they can be seen) and are marked with a zig-\/zag pattern to indicate that you need to zoom in to see more detail.

The zig-\/zag pattern can be seen applied to frame sets on figure 1717, and zones on figure 2020.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1017}{}\doxysubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Time scale}{Time scale}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1017}
The time scale is a quick aid in determining the relation between screen space and the time it represents (figure 1616).

$<$figure id="{}timescale"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Time scale.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

The leftmost value on the scale represents when the timeline starts. The rest of the numbers label the notches on the scale, with some numbers omitted if there\textquotesingle{}s no space to display them.

Hovering the  mouse pointer over the time scale will display a tooltip with the exact timestamp at the position of the mouse cursor.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_framesets}{}\doxysubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Frame sets}{Frame sets}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_framesets}
Frames from each frame set are displayed directly underneath the time scale. Each frame set occupies a separate row. The currently selected frame set is highlighted with bright colors, with the rest dimmed out.

$<$figure id="{}framesetsfig"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Frames on the timeline.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

In figure 1717 we can see the fully described frames 312 and 347. The description consists of the frame name, which is {\itshape Frame} for the default frame set (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_markingframes}{3.3}{2}3.\+3) or the name you used for the secondary name set (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_secondaryframeset}{3.3.1}{3}3.\+3.\+1), the frame number, and the frame time. Since frame 348 is too small to be fully labeled, only the frame time is shown. On the other hand, frame 349 is even smaller, with no space for any text. Moreover, frames 313 to 346 are too small to be displayed individually, so they are replaced with a zig-\/zag pattern, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collapseditems}{5.2.3.0.1}{5}5.\+2.\+3.\+0.\+1.

You can also see frame separators are projected down to the rest of the timeline view. Note that only the separators for the currently selected frame set are displayed. You can make a frame set active by clicking the left mouse button on a frame set row you want to select (also see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_controlmenu}{5.2.1}{3}5.\+2.\+1).

Clicking the middle mouse button on a frame will zoom the view to the extent of the frame.

If a frame has an associated frame image (see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frameimages}{3.3.3}{3}3.\+3.\+3), you can hold the Ctrl key and click the left mouse button on the frame to open the frame image playback window (see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_playback}{5.20}{2}5.\+20) and set the playback to the selected frame.

If the {\itshape  Draw frame targets} option is enabled (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4), time regions in frames exceeding the set target value will be marked with a red background.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Flag Checkered icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1020}{}\doxysubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Sections}{Sections}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1020}
If sections of program execution were marked (see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_markingsections}{3.5}{2}3.\+5), the profiler will try to reconstruct a child-\/parent hierarchy between the sections, as presented on figure 1818.

$<$figure id="{}figsections"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Sections showing a hierarchy.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

With some data sets such reconstruction will not be possible, in which case sections may look as on figure 1919.

$<$figure id="{}figsections2"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Sections that cannot form a hierarchy.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

Clicking the middle mouse button on a section will zoom the view to the extent of the section.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneslocksplots}{}\doxysubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Zones, locks and plots display}{Zones, locks and plots display}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneslocksplots}
You will find the zones with locks and their associated threads on this combined view. The plots are graphed right below.

$<$figure id="{}zoneslocks"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Zones and locks display.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

The left-\/hand side {\itshape index area} of the timeline view displays various labels (threads, locks), which can be categorized in the following way:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Light blue label} -- GPU context. Multi-\/threaded Vulkan, Open\+CL, Direct3D 12, Metal and Web\+GPU contexts are additionally split into separate threads.
\item {\itshape Pink label} -- CPU data graph.
\item {\itshape White label} -- A CPU thread. It will be replaced by a bright red label in a thread that has crashed (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_crashhandling}{2.5}{2}2.\+5
\end{DoxyItemize}). If automated sampling was performed, clicking the left mouse button on the {\itshape  ghost zones} button will switch zone display mode between "{}instrumented"{} and "{}ghost."{}


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Green label} -- Fiber, coroutine, or any other sort of cooperative multitasking "{}green thread."{}
\item {\itshape Light red label} -- Indicates a lock.
\item {\itshape Yellow label} -- Plot.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Labels accompanied by the  symbol can be collapsed out of the view to reduce visual clutter. Hover the  mouse pointer over the label to display additional information. Click the middle mouse button on a title to zoom the view to the extent of the label contents. Finally, click the right mouse button on a label to display the context menu with available actions:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Hide} -- Hides the label along with the content associated to it. To make the label visible again, you must find it in the options menu (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4
\end{DoxyItemize}).

Under the  symbol are a series of points that allow to limit the depth of the zones displayed. Hover the  mouse pointer over a circle to display a line visualizing the cutting point, then click the middle mouse button to apply or remove a zone depth limit.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Ghost icon  -\/ Caret Down icon  -\/ Arrow Pointer icon  -\/ Eye Slash icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1022}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Zones}{Zones}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1022}
In an example in figure 2020 you can see that there are two threads:\+ {\itshape Main thread} and {\itshape Streaming thread}\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}76]\+. We can see that the {\itshape Main thread} has two root level zones visible:\+ {\itshape Update} and {\itshape Render}. The {\itshape Update} zone is split into further sub-\/zones, some of which are too small to be displayed at the current zoom level. This is indicated by drawing a zig-\/zag pattern over the merged zones box (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collapseditems}{5.2.3.0.1}{5}5.\+2.\+3.\+0.\+1), with the number of collapsed zones printed in place of the zone name. We can also see that the {\itshape Physics} zone acquires the {\itshape Physics lock} mutex for most of its run time.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}76]\+:\+ By clicking on a thread name, you can temporarily disable the display of the zones in this thread.

Meanwhile, the {\itshape Streaming thread} is performing some {\itshape Streaming jobs}. The first {\itshape Streaming job} sent a message (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_messagelog}{3.8}{2}3.\+8). In addition to being listed in the message log, it is indicated by a triangle over the thread separator. When multiple messages are in one place, the triangle outline shape changes to a filled triangle.

The GPU zones are displayed just like CPU zones, with an Open\+GL /\+ Vulkan /\+ Direct3D /\+ Metal /\+ Open\+CL /\+ CUDA /\+ Web\+GPU context in place of a thread name.

Hovering the  mouse pointer over a zone will highlight all other zones that have the exact source location with a white outline. Clicking the left mouse button on a zone will open the zone information window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneinfo}{5.15}{2}5.\+15). Holding the Ctrl key and clicking the left mouse button on a zone will open the zone statistics window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7). Clicking the middle mouse button on a zone will zoom the view to the extent of the zone.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1024}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Ghost zones}{Ghost zones}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1024}
You can enable the view of ghost zones (not pictured on figure 2020, but similar to standard zones view) by clicking on the {\itshape  ghost zones} icon next to the thread label, available if automated sampling (see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sampling}{3.18.5}{3}3.\+18.\+5) was performed. Ghost zones will also be displayed by default if no instrumented zones are available for a given thread to help with pinpointing functions that should be instrumented.

Ghost zones represent true function calls in the program, periodically reported by the operating system. Due to the limited sampling resolution, you need to take great care when looking at reported timing data. While it may be apparent that some small function requires a relatively long time to execute, for example, 125 μs (8 k\+Hz sampling rate), in reality, this time represents a period between taking two distinct samples, not the actual function run time. Similarly, two (or more) separate function calls may be represented as a single ghost zone because the profiler doesn\textquotesingle{}t have the information needed to know about the actual lifetime of a sampled function.

Another common pitfall to watch for is the order of presented functions. {\itshape It is not what you expect it to be!} Read chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_readingcallstacks}{5.16.1}{3}5.\+16.\+1 for critical insight on how call stacks might seem nonsensical at first and why they aren\textquotesingle{}t.

The available information about ghost zones is quite limited, but it\textquotesingle{}s enough to give you a rough outlook on the execution of your application. The timeline view alone is more than any other statistical profiler can present. In addition, Tracy correctly handles inlined function calls, which are indicated by a darker background of ghost zones. Lastly, zones representing kernel-\/mode functions are displayed with red function names.

Clicking the left mouse button on a ghost zone will open the corresponding source file location, if able (see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sourceview}{5.17}{2}5.\+17 for conditions). There are three ways in which source locations can be assigned to a ghost zone:\+


\begin{DoxyEnumerate}
\item If the selected ghost zone is {\itshape not} an inline frame and its symbol data has been retrieved, the source location points to the function entry location (first line of the function).
\item If the selected ghost zone is {\itshape not} an inline frame, but its symbol data is not available, the source location will point to a semi-\/random location within the function body (i.\+e. to one of the sampled addresses in the program, but not necessarily the one representing the selected time stamp, as multiple samples with different addresses may be merged into one ghost zone).
\item If the selected ghost zone {\itshape is} an inline frame, the source location will point to a semi-\/random location within the inlined function body (see details in the above point). It is impossible to go to such a function\textquotesingle{}s entry location, as it doesn\textquotesingle{}t exist in the program binary. Inlined functions begin in the parent function.
\end{DoxyEnumerate}

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Ghost icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1026}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Call stack samples}{Call stack samples}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1026}
The row of dots right below the thread label ({\itshape Main thread} in the example) shows call stack sample points, which may have been automatically captured (see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sampling}{3.18.5}{3}3.\+18.\+5 for more detail). Each sample is color-\/coded as follows:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Green} -- shows samples inside the profiled program.
\item {\itshape Blue} -- indicates samples belonging to external libraries.
\item {\itshape Red} -- used for samples captured in the kernel.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Hovering the  mouse pointer over each dot displays a short call stack summary, while clicking the dot with the left mouse button opens a more detailed call stack information window (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstackwindow}{5.16}{2}5.\+16).

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_context-switches}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Context switches}{Context switches}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_context-switches}
The thick line right below the samples represents context switch data (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_contextswitches}{3.18.3}{3}3.\+18.\+3). We can see that the main thread, as displayed, starts in a suspended state, represented by the dotted region. Then it is woken up and starts execution of the {\ttfamily Update} zone. It is preempted amid the physics processing, which explains why there is an empty space between child zones. Then it is resumed again and continues execution into the {\ttfamily Render} zone, where it is preempted again, but for a shorter time. After rendering is done, the thread sleeps again, presumably waiting for the vertical blanking to indicate the next frame. Similar information is also available for the streaming thread.

Context switch regions are using the following color key:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Green} -- Thread is running.
\item {\itshape Red} -- Thread is waiting to be resumed by the scheduler. There are many reasons why a thread may be in the waiting state. Hovering the  mouse pointer over the region will display more information. If sampling was performed, the profiler might display a wait stack. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_waitstacks}{3.18.5.1}{4}3.\+18.\+5.\+1
\end{DoxyItemize}for additional details.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Blue} -- Thread is waiting to be resumed and is migrating to another CPU core. This might have visible performance effects because low-\/level CPU caches are not shared between cores, which may result in additional cache misses. To avoid this problem, you may pin a thread to a specific core by setting its affinity.
\item {\itshape Bronze} -- Thread has been placed in the scheduler\textquotesingle{}s run queue and is about to be resumed.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Fiber work and yield states are presented in the same way as context switch regions.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1029}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{CPU data}{CPU data}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1029}
This label is only available if the profiler collected context switch data. It is split into two parts:\+ a graph of CPU load by various threads running in the system and a per-\/core thread execution display.

The CPU load graph shows how much CPU resources were used at any given time during program execution. The green part of the graph represents threads belonging to the profiled application, and the gray part of the graph shows all other programs running in the system. Hovering the  mouse pointer over the graph will display a list of threads running on the CPU at the given time.

Each line in the thread execution display represents a separate logical CPU thread. If CPU topology data is available (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_cputopology}{3.18.4}{3}3.\+18.\+4), package and core assignment will be displayed in brackets, in addition to numerical processor identifier (i.\+e. {\ttfamily \+[}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}{\ttfamily package}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}{\ttfamily :\+}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}{\ttfamily \doxylink{group__core}{Core features}}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}{\ttfamily ]\+ CPU }\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}{\ttfamily thread}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}). When a core is busy executing a thread, a zone will be drawn at the appropriate time. Zones are colored according to the following key:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Bright color} -- or {\itshape orange} if dynamic thread colors are disabled -- Thread tracked by the profiler.
\item {\itshape Dark blue} -- Thread existing in the profiled application but not known to the profiler. This may include internal profiler threads, helper threads created by external libraries, etc.
\item {\itshape Gray} -- Threads assigned to other programs running in the system.
\end{DoxyItemize}

When the  mouse pointer is hovered over either the CPU data zone or the thread timeline label, Tracy will display a line connecting all zones associated with the selected thread. This can be used to quickly see how the thread migrated across the CPU cores.

It will also add lines starting with a filed circle to denote wake up events. Those are useful to pinpoint the origin of a thread waking up, especially when holding locks. It may also start from an empty region, denoting the time at which the kernel chose to schedule or boost the priority of your thread. Wake ups will have a different color based on the reason for which the thread was waiting to be scheduled.

$<$figure id="{}threadmigration"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Thread migration and wake up.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

In the above picture, {\itshape Thread B} migrates from {\itshape Core 3} to {\itshape Core 4} due to a wake up from {\itshape Thread A}. Then it migrates from {\itshape Core 4} to {\itshape Core 1}.

Clicking the left mouse button on a tracked thread will make it visible on the timeline if it was either hidden or collapsed before. It will also lock the selected thread so that you may pan and explore data while retaining the visualization of thread migrations and wake up events.
