Clicking again somewhere empty on the timeline with the left mouse button will unlock the selection.

Careful examination of the data presented on this graph may allow you to determine areas where the profiled application was fighting for system resources with other programs (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_checkenvironmentos}{2.2.1}{3}2.\+2.\+1) or give you a hint to add more instrumentation macros.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1031}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Locks}{Locks}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1031}
Mutual exclusion zones are displayed in each thread that tries to acquire them. There are three color-\/coded kinds of lock event regions that may be displayed. Note that the contention regions are always displayed over the uncontented ones when the timeline view is zoomed out.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Green region\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}77]\+} -- The lock is being held solely by one thread, and no other thread tries to access it. In the case of shared locks, multiple threads hold the read lock, but no thread requires a write lock.
\item {\itshape Yellow region} -- The lock is being owned by this thread, and some other thread also wants to acquire the lock.
\item {\itshape Red region} -- The thread wants to acquire the lock but is blocked by other thread or threads in case of a shared lock.
\end{DoxyItemize}

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}77]\+:\+ This region type is disabled by default and needs to be enabled in options (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{5.4}{2}5.\+4).

Hovering the  mouse pointer over a lock timeline will highlight the lock in all threads to help read the lock behavior. Hovering the  mouse pointer over a lock event will display important information, for example, a list of threads that are currently blocking or which are blocked by the lock. Clicking the left mouse button on a lock event or a lock label will open the lock information window, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_lockwindow}{5.19}{2}5.\+19. Clicking the middle mouse button on a lock event will zoom the view to the extent of the event.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1033}{}\doxysubsubsubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Plots}{Plots}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1033}
The numerical data values (figure 2222) are plotted right below the zones and locks. Note that the minimum and maximum values currently displayed on the plot are visible on the screen, along with the y range of the plot and the number of drawn data points. The discrete data points are indicated with little rectangles. A filled rectangle indicates multiple data points.

$<$figure id="{}plotdisplay"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Plot display.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

When memory profiling (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memoryprofiling}{3.9}{2}3.\+9) is enabled, Tracy will automatically generate a {\itshape  Memory usage} plot, which has extended capabilities. For example, hovering over a data point (memory allocation event) will visually display the allocation duration. Clicking the left mouse button on the data point will open the memory allocation information window, which will show the duration of the allocation as long as the window is open.

Another plot that Tracy automatically provides is the {\itshape  CPU usage} plot, which represents the total system CPU usage percentage (it is not limited to the profiled application).

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Memory icon  -\/ Gauge High icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1035}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Navigating the view}{Navigating the view}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1035}
Hovering the  mouse pointer over the timeline view will display a vertical line that you can use to line up events in multiple threads visually. Dragging the left mouse button will display the time measurement of the selected region.

The timeline view may be scrolled both vertically and horizontally by dragging the right mouse button. Note that only the zones, locks, and plots scroll vertically, while the time scale and frame sets always stay on the top.

You can zoom in and out the timeline view by using the mouse wheel. Pressing the Ctrl key will make zooming more precise while pressing the Shift key will make it faster. You can select a range to which you want to zoom in by dragging the middle mouse button. Dragging the middle mouse button while the Ctrl key is pressed will zoom out.

It is also possible to navigate the timeline using the keyboard. The A and D keys scroll the view to the left and right, respectively. The W and S keys change the zoom level.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timeranges}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Time ranges}{Time ranges}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timeranges}
Sometimes, you may want to specify a time range, such as limiting some statistics to a specific part of your program execution or marking interesting places.

To define a time range, drag the left mouse button over the timeline view while holding the Ctrl key. When the mouse key is released, the profiler will mark the selected time extent with a blue striped pattern, and it will display a context menu with the following options:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item  Set time range for:\+
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Find zone} -- this will limit find zone results. See chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyItemize}for more details.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Statistics} -- selecting this option will limit statistics results. See chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_statistics}{5.6}{2}5.\+6
\end{DoxyItemize}for more details.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Flame graph} -- limits flame graph results. Refer to chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_flamegraph}{5.9}{2}5.\+9
\end{DoxyItemize}.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Wait stacks} -- limits wait stacks results. Refer to chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_stackwindows}{5.18}{2}5.\+18
\end{DoxyItemize}.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Memory} -- limits memory results. Read more about this in chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memorywindow}{5.10}{2}5.\+10
\end{DoxyItemize}.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Frame statistics} -- limits frame statistics. Section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_framestatistics}{5.14}{2}5.\+14
\end{DoxyItemize}has more information.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Add annotation} -- use to annotate regions of interest, as described in chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_annotatingtrace}{5.3.1}{3}5.\+3.\+1
\end{DoxyItemize}.

Alternatively, you may specify the time range by clicking the right mouse button on a zone, section or a frame. The resulting time extent will match the selected item.

To reduce clutter, time range regions are only displayed if the windows they affect are open or if the time range limits control window is open (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timerangelimits}{5.24}{2}5.\+24). You can access the time range limits window through the {\itshape  Tools} button on the control menu. Time range limits can also be disabled or enabled in the windows showing the data they affect.

You can freely adjust each time range on the timeline by clicking the left mouse button on the range\textquotesingle{}s edge and dragging the mouse.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Ruler icon  -\/ Magnifying Glass icon  -\/ Arrow Up Wide Short icon  -\/ Fire Flame Curved icon  -\/ Hourglass Half icon  -\/ Memory icon  -\/ Images icon  -\/ Note Sticky icon  -\/ Screwdriver Wrench icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_annotatingtrace}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Annotating the trace}{Annotating the trace}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_annotatingtrace}
Tracy allows adding custom notes to the trace. For example, you may want to mark a region to ignore because the application was out-\/of-\/focus or a region where a new user was connecting to the game, which resulted in a frame drop that needs to be investigated.

Methods of specifying the annotation region are described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timeranges}{5.3}{2}5.\+3. When a new annotation is added, it is assigned a semi-\/unique random name to make it distinguishable. The settings window is also opened (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_annotationsettings}{5.22}{2}5.\+22), allowing you to enter your own description of the annotation.

Annotations are displayed on the timeline, as presented in figure 2323. Clicking on the text description area will open the annotation settings window, in which you can modify or remove the region. List of all annotations in the trace is available in the annotations list window described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_annotationlist}{5.23}{2}5.\+23, which is accessible through the {\itshape  Tools} button on the control menu.

$<$figure id="{}annotation"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Annotation region.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

Please note that while the annotations persist between profiling sessions, they are not saved in the trace but in the trace sidecar file, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_tracespecific}{9.2}{2}9.\+2.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Screwdriver Wrench icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Options menu}{Options menu}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_options}
In this window, you can set various trace-\/related options. For example, the timeline view might sometimes become overcrowded, in which case disabling the display of some profiling events can increase readability.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw empty labels} -- By default threads that don\textquotesingle{}t have anything to display at the current zoom level are hidden. Enabling this option will show them anyway.
\item {\itshape  Draw frame targets} -- If enabled, time regions in any frame from the currently selected frame set, which exceed the specified {\itshape Target FPS} value will be marked with a red background on timeline view.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Target FPS} -- Controls the option above, but also the frame bar colors in the frame time graph (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frametimegraph}{5.2.2}{3}5.\+2.\+2
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyItemize}). The color range thresholds are presented in a line directly below.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw context switches} -- Allows disabling context switch display in threads.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Darken inactive thread} -- If enabled, inactive regions in threads will be dimmed out.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw CPU data} -- Per-\/\+CPU behavior graph can be disabled here.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw CPU usage graph} -- You can disable drawing of the CPU usage graph here.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw GPU zones} -- Allows disabling display of Open\+GL/\+\+Vulkan/\+\+Metal/\+\+Direct3\+D/\+\+Open\+CL/\+\+CUDA/\+\+Web\+GPU zones. The {\itshape GPU zones} drop-\/down allows disabling individual GPU contexts and setting CPU/\+\+GPU drift offsets of uncalibrated contexts (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_gpuprofiling}{3.10}{2}3.\+10
\end{DoxyItemize}for more information). The {\itshape  Auto} button automatically measures the GPU drift value\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}78]\+.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw CPU zones} -- Determines whether CPU zones are displayed.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw ghost zones} -- Controls if ghost zones should be displayed in threads which don\textquotesingle{}t have any instrumented zones available.
\item {\itshape  Zone colors} -- Zones with no user-\/set color may be colored according to the following schemes:\+
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Disabled} -- A constant color (blue) will be used.
\item {\itshape Thread dynamic} -- Zones are colored according to a thread (identifier number) they belong to and depth level.
\item {\itshape Source location dynamic} -- Zone color is determined by source location (function name) and depth level.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Enabling the {\itshape Ignore custom} option will force usage of the selected zone coloring scheme, disregarding any colors set by the user in profiled code. Enabling the {\itshape Inherit parent colors} option will cause zones that have a color set by the user in the profiled code to be propagated down to the child zones, although slightly darker.
\item {\itshape  Zone name shortening} -- controls display behavior of long zone names, which don\textquotesingle{}t fit inside a zone box:\+
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Disabled} -- Shortening of zone names is not performed and names are always displayed in full (e.\+g.\+ {\ttfamily bool ns::\+container\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}float\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}::add(const float\&)}).
\item {\itshape Minimal length} -- Always reduces zone name to minimal length, even if there is space available for a longer form (e.\+g.\+ {\ttfamily add()}).
\item {\itshape Only normalize} -- Only performs normalization of the zone name\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}79]\+, but does not remove namespaces (e.\+g.\+ {\ttfamily ns::\+container\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}::add()}).
\item {\itshape As needed} -- Name shortening steps will be performed only if there is no space to display a complete zone name, and only until the name fits available space, or shortening is no longer possible (e.\+g.\+ {\ttfamily container\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}::add()}).
\item {\itshape As needed + normalize} -- Same as above, but zone name normalization will always be performed, even if the entire zone name fits in the space available.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Function names in the remaining places across the UI will be normalized unless this option is set to {\itshape Disabled}.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw locks} -- Controls the display of locks. If the {\itshape Only contended} option is selected, the profiler won\textquotesingle{}t display the non-\/blocking regions of locks (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneslocksplots}{5.2.3.4}{4}5.\+2.\+3.\+4
\end{DoxyItemize}). The {\itshape Locks} drop-\/down allows disabling the display of locks on a per-\/lock basis. As a convenience, the list of locks is split into the single-\/threaded and multi-\/threaded (contended and uncontended) categories. Clicking the right mouse button on a lock label opens the lock information window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_lockwindow}{5.19}{2}5.\+19).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Draw plots} -- Allows disabling display of plots. Individual plots can be disabled in the {\itshape Plots} drop-\/down. The vertical size of the plots can be adjusted using the {\itshape Plot heights} slider.
\item {\itshape  Visible threads} -- Here you can select which threads are visible on the timeline. You can change the display order of threads by dragging thread labels. Threads can be sorted alphabetically with the {\itshape Sort} button.
\item {\itshape  Visible frame sets} -- Frame set display can be enabled or disabled here. Note that disabled frame sets are still available for selection in the frame set selection drop-\/down (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_controlmenu}{5.2.1}{3}5.\+2.\+1
\end{DoxyItemize}) but are marked with a dimmed font.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}78]\+:\+ There is an assumption that drift is linear. Automated measurement calculates and removes change over time in delay-\/to-\/execution of GPU zones. Resulting value may still be incorrect.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}79]\+:\+ The normalization process removes the function {\ttfamily const} qualifier, some common return type declarations and all function parameters and template arguments.

Disabling the display of some events is especially recommended when the profiler performance drops below acceptable levels for interactive usage.

It is possible to store defaults for the settings marked with a {\itshape \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}} to the global Tracy configuration file. This can be done using the {\itshape Save current options as defaults} button at the bottom of the window, or by manually editing this configuration file (for which the path is indicated in the tooltip). Next time you use Tracy, these stored default options will be used instead. For now, restoring the defaults can be done by deleting the configuration file.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Expand icon  -\/ Flag Checkered icon  -\/ Person Hiking icon  -\/ Moon icon  -\/ Sliders icon  -\/ Signature icon  -\/ Eye icon  -\/ Robot icon  -\/ Microchip icon  -\/ Ghost icon  -\/ Palette icon  -\/ Ruler Horizontal icon  -\/ Lock icon  -\/ Shuffle icon  -\/ Images icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_messages}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Messages window}{Messages window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_messages}
In this window, you can see all the messages that were sent by the client application, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_messagelog}{3.8}{2}3.\+8. The window is split into four columns:\+ {\itshape time}, {\itshape thread}, {\itshape message} and {\itshape call stack}. Hovering the  mouse cursor over a message will highlight it on the timeline view. Clicking the left mouse button on a message will center the timeline view on the selected message.

The {\itshape call stack} column is filled only if a call stack capture was requested, as described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collectingcallstacks}{3.12}{2}3.\+12. A single entry consists of the {\itshape  Show} button, which opens the call stack information window (chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstackwindow}{5.16}{2}5.\+16) and of abbreviated information about the call path.

If the {\itshape  Show frame images} option is selected, hovering the  mouse cursor over a message will show a tooltip containing frame image (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frameimages}{3.3.3}{3}3.\+3.\+3) associated with a frame in which the message was issued, if available.

The message list will automatically scroll down to display the most recent message during live capture. You can disable this behavior by manually scrolling the message list up. The auto-\/scrolling feature will be enabled again when the view is scrolled down to display the last message.

You can filter the message list in the following ways:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item By the originating thread in the {\itshape  Visible threads} drop-\/down.
\item By matching the message text to the expression in the {\itshape  Filter messages} entry field. Multiple filter expressions can be comma-\/separated (e.\+g. "{}warn, info"{} will match messages containing strings "{}warn"{} {\itshape or} "{}info"{}). You can exclude matches by preceding the term with a minus character (e.\+g., "{}-\/debug"{} will hide all messages containing the string "{}debug"{}).
\item By message source, distinguishing between {\itshape  User} messages and internal {\itshape  Tracy} diagnostics.
\item By severity level:\+ {\itshape  Trace}, {\itshape  Debug}, {\itshape  Info}, {\itshape  Warning}, {\itshape  Error}, or {\itshape  Fatal}.
\end{DoxyItemize}

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Arrow Pointer icon  -\/ Align Justify icon  -\/ Image icon  -\/ Shuffle icon  -\/ Filter icon  -\/ User icon  -\/ Microscope icon  -\/ Shoe Prints icon  -\/ Bug icon  -\/ Info icon  -\/ Triangle Exclamation icon  -\/ Circle Xmark icon  -\/ Skull Crossbones icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_statistics}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Statistics window}{Statistics window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_statistics}
Looking at the timeline view gives you a very localized outlook on things. However, sometimes you want to look at the general overview of the program\textquotesingle{}s behavior. For example, you want to know which function takes the most of the application\textquotesingle{}s execution time. The statistics window provides you with exactly that information.

If the trace capture was performed with call stack sampling enabled (as described in chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sampling}{3.18.5}{3}3.\+18.\+5), you will be presented with an option to switch between {\itshape  Instrumentation} and {\itshape  Sampling} modes. If the profiler collected no sampling data, but it retrieved symbols, the second mode will be displayed as {\itshape  Symbols}, enabling you to list available symbols.

If GPU zones were captured, you would also have the {\itshape  GPU} option to view the GPU zones statistics.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Syringe icon  -\/ Eye Dropper icon  -\/ Puzzle Piece icon  -\/ Eye icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1042}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Instrumentation mode}{Instrumentation mode}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1042}
Here you will find a multi-\/column display of captured zones, which contains:\+ the zone {\itshape name} and {\itshape location}, {\itshape total time} spent in the zone, the {\itshape count} of zone executions, the {\itshape mean time spent in the zone per call} and the number of threads the zone has appeared in, labeled with a {\itshape  thread icon}. You may sort the view according to the four displayed values or by the name.

In the {\itshape  \+Timing} menu, the {\itshape  \+With children} selection displays inclusive measurements, that is, containing execution time of zone\textquotesingle{}s children. The {\itshape  \+Self only} selection switches the measurement to exclusive, displaying just the time spent in the zone, subtracting the child calls. Finally, the {\itshape  \+Non-\/reentrant} selection shows inclusive time but counts only the first appearance of a given zone on a thread\textquotesingle{}s stack.

Clicking the left mouse button on a zone will open the individual zone statistics view in the find zone window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7).

You can filter the displayed list of zones by matching the zone name to the expression in the {\itshape  Filter zones} entry field. Refer to section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_messages}{5.5}{2}5.\+5 for a more detailed description of the expression syntax.

To limit the statistics to a specific time extent, you may enable the {\itshape Limit range} option (chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timeranges}{5.3}{2}5.\+3). The inclusion region will be marked with a red striped pattern. Note that a zone must be entirely inside the region to be counted. You can access more options through the {\itshape  Limits} button, which will open the time range limits window, described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timerangelimits}{5.24}{2}5.\+24.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Shuffle icon  -\/ Filter icon  -\/ Ruler icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_statisticssampling}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Sampling mode}{Sampling mode}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_statisticssampling}
Data displayed in this mode is, in essence, very similar to the instrumentation one. Here you will find function names, their locations in source code, and time measurements. There are, however, some significant differences.

First and foremost, the presented information is constructed from many call stack samples, which represent real addresses in the application\textquotesingle{}s binary code, mapped to the line numbers in the source files. This reverse mapping may not always be possible or could be erroneous. Furthermore, due to the nature of the sampling process, it is impossible to obtain exact time measurements. Instead, time values are guesstimated by multiplying the number of sample counts by mean time between two different samples.

The sample statistics list symbols, not functions. These terms are similar but not exactly the same. A symbol always has a base function that gives it its name. In most cases, a symbol will also contain a number of inlined functions. In some cases, the same function may be inlined more than once within the same symbol. Inspecting the local call stacks displayed in tooltips will show the specific paths by which these inlines were called within the symbol. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_assemblymode}{5.17.2.2}{4}5.\+17.\+2.\+2 for more detail.

The {\itshape Name} column contains name of the symbol in which the sampling was done. Kernel-\/mode symbol samples are distinguished with the red color. Symbols containing inlined functions are listed with the number of inlined functions in parentheses and can be expanded to show all inlined functions (some functions may be hidden if the {\itshape  Show all} option is disabled due to lack of sampling data). Clicking the left mouse button on a function name will open a popup with options to select:\+ you can either open the symbol view window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_symbolview}{5.17.2}{3}5.\+17.\+2), or the sample entry stacks window (see chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_stackwindows}{5.18}{2}5.\+18)\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}80]\+.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}80]\+:\+ Note that if inclusive times are displayed, listed functions will be partially or completely coming from mid-\/stack frames, preventing, or limiting the capability to display the data.

By default, each inlining of a function is listed separately. If you prefer to combine the measurements for functions that are inlined multiple times within a function, you can do so by enabling the {\itshape  Aggregate} option. You cannot view sample entry stacks of inlined functions when this grouping method is enabled.

In some cases it may be more interesting to see the most time consuming inline within the symbol rather than the symbol name. If you enable the {\itshape  Top inline} option, the name of the busiest inline function will be displayed in the {\itshape Name} column.

If the {\itshape  Inlines} option is enabled, the list will show all functions without grouping them by symbol. In this mode, inline functions are preceded by a  symbol and their parent function name is displayed in parentheses.

The {\itshape Location} column displays the corresponding source file name and line number. Depending on the {\itshape Location} option selection, it can either show the function entry address or the instruction at which the sampling was performed. The {\itshape Entry} mode points at the beginning of a non-\/inlined function or at the place where the compiler inserted an inlined function in its parent function. The {\itshape Sample} mode is not useful for non-\/inlined functions, as it points to one randomly selected sampling point out of many that were captured. However, in the case of inlined functions, this random sampling point is within the inlined function body. Using these options in tandem lets you look at both the inlined function code and the place where it was inserted. If the {\itshape Smart} location is selected, the profiler will display the entry point position for non-\/inlined functions and sample location for inlined functions. Selecting the {\itshape @ Address} option will instead print the symbol address.

The location data is complemented by the originating executable image name, contained in the {\itshape Image} column. If the {\itshape  Short images} option is selected, the image path will be shortened to just the image file name, with the full path available in the tooltip.

The profiler may not find some function locations due to insufficient debugging data available on the client-\/side. To filter out such entries, use the {\itshape  Hide unknown} option.

The {\itshape Time} or {\itshape Count} column (depending on the {\itshape  Show time} option selection) shows number of taken samples, either as a raw count, or in an easier to understand time format. Note that the percentage value of time is calculated relative to the wall-\/clock time. The percentage value of sample counts is relative to the total number of collected samples. You can also make the percentages of inline functions relative to the base symbol measurements by enabling the {\itshape  Base relative} option.

The last column, {\itshape Code size}, displays the size of the symbol in the executable image of the program. Since inlined routines are directly embedded into other functions, their symbol size will be based on the parent symbol and displayed as \textquotesingle{}less than\textquotesingle{}. In some cases, this data won\textquotesingle{}t be available. If the symbol code has been retrieved\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}81]\+ symbol size will be prepended with the {\ttfamily } icon, and clicking the right mouse button on the location column entry will open symbol view window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_symbolview}{5.17.2}{3}5.\+17.\+2).

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}81]\+:\+ Symbols larger than 128 \+KB are not captured.

Finally, the list can be filtered using the {\itshape  Filter symbols} entry field, just like in the instrumentation mode case. Additionally, you can also filter results by the originating image name of the symbol. You may disable the display of kernel symbols with the {\itshape  Kernel} switch. Symbols from external libraries are hidden by default; enable the {\itshape  External} toggle to show them. The exclusive/\+inclusive time counting mode can be switched using the {\itshape  \+Timing} menu (non-\/reentrant timing is not available in the Sampling view). Limiting the time range is also available but is restricted to self-\/time. If the {\itshape  Show all} option is selected, the list will include not only the call stack samples but also all other symbols collected during the profiling process (this is enabled by default if no sampling was performed).

A simple CSV document containing the visible zones after filtering and limiting can be copied to the clipboard with the button adjacent to the visible zones count. The document contains the following columns:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily name} -- Zone name
\item {\ttfamily src\+\_\+file} -- Source file where the zone was set
\item {\ttfamily src\+\_\+line} -- \doxylink{struct_line}{Line} in the source file where the zone was set
\item {\ttfamily total\+\_\+ns} -- Total zone time in nanoseconds
\item {\ttfamily counts} -- Zone count
\end{DoxyItemize}

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Puzzle Piece icon  -\/ Layer Group icon  -\/ Fire icon  -\/ Sitemap icon  -\/ Caret Right icon  -\/ Scissors icon  -\/ Eye Slash icon  -\/ Stopwatch icon  -\/ Link icon  -\/ Database icon  -\/ Filter icon  -\/ Hat Wizard icon  -\/ Shield Halved icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1045}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{GPU zones mode}{GPU zones mode}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1045}
This is an analog of the instrumentation mode, but for the GPU zones. Note that the available options may be limited here.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Find zone window}{Find zone window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}
The individual behavior of zones may be influenced by many factors, like CPU cache effects, access times amortized by the disk cache, thread context switching, etc. Moreover, sometimes the execution time depends on the internal data structures and their response to different inputs. In other words, it is hard to determine the actual performance characteristics by looking at any single zone.

Tracy gives you the ability to display an execution time histogram of all occurrences of a zone. On this view, you can see how the function behaves in general. You can inspect how various data inputs influence the execution time. You can filter the data to eventually drill down to the individual zone calls to see the environment in which they were called.

You start by entering a search query, which will be matched against known zone names (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_markingzones}{3.4}{2}3.\+4 for information on the grouping of zone names). If the search found some results, you will be presented with a list of zones in the {\itshape matched source locations} drop-\/down. The selected zone\textquotesingle{}s graph is displayed on the {\itshape histogram} drop-\/down, and also the matching zones are highlighted on the timeline view.

Clicking the right mouse button on the source file location will open the source file view window (if applicable, see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sourceview}{5.17}{2}5.\+17). If symbol data is available Tracy will try to match the instrumented zone name to a captured symbol. If this succeeds and there are no duplicate matches, the source file view will be accompanied by the disassembly of the code. Since this matching is not exact, in rare cases you may get the wrong data here. To just display the source code, press and hold the Ctrl key while clicking the right mouse button.

An example histogram is presented in figure 2424. Here you can see that the majority of zone calls (by count) are clustered in the 300 ns group, closely followed by the 10 μs cluster. There are some outliers at the 1 and 10 ms marks, which can be ignored on most occasions, as these are single occurrences.

$<$figure id="{}findzonehistogram"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Zone execution time histogram. Note that the extreme time labels and time range indicator (middle time value) are displayed in a separate line.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

Various data statistics about displayed data accompany the histogram, for example, the {\itshape total time} of the displayed samples or the {\itshape maximum number of counts} in histogram bins. The following options control how the data is presented:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Log values} -- Switches between linear and logarithmic scale on the y axis of the graph, representing the call counts\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}82]\+.
\item {\itshape Log time} -- Switches between linear and logarithmic scale on the x axis of the graph, representing the time bins.
\item {\itshape Cumulate time} -- Changes how the histogram bin values are calculated. By default, the vertical bars on the graph represent the {\itshape call counts} of zones that fit in the given time bin. If this option is enabled, the bars represent the {\itshape time spent} in the zones. For example, on the graph presented in figure 2424
\end{DoxyItemize}the 10 μs cluster is the dominating one, if we look at the time spent in the zone, even if the 300 ns cluster has a greater number of call counts.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Self time} -- Removes children time from the analyzed zones, which results in displaying only the time spent in the zone itself (or in non-\/instrumented function calls). It cannot be selected when {\itshape Running time} is active.
\item {\itshape Running time} -- Removes time when zone\textquotesingle{}s thread execution was suspended by the operating system due to preemption by other threads, waiting for system resources, lock contention, etc. Available only when the profiler performed context switch capture (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_contextswitches}{3.18.3}{3}3.\+18.\+3
\end{DoxyItemize}). It cannot be selected when {\itshape Self time} is active.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Minimum values in bin} -- Excludes display of bins that do not hold enough values at both ends of the time range. Increasing this parameter will eliminate outliers, allowing us to concentrate on the interesting part of the graph.
\end{DoxyItemize}

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}82]\+:\+ Or time, if the {\itshape cumulate time} option is enabled.

You can drag the left mouse button over the histogram to select a time range that you want to look at closely. This will display the data in the histogram info section, and it will also filter zones shown in the {\itshape found zones} section. This is quite useful if you actually want to look at the outliers, i.\+e., where did they originate from, what the program was doing at the moment, etc\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}83]\+. You can reset the selection range by pressing the right mouse button on the histogram.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}83]\+:\+ More often than not you will find out, that the application was just starting, or access to a cold file was required and there\textquotesingle{}s not much you can do to optimize that particular case.

The {\itshape found zones} section displays the individual zones grouped according to the following criteria:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Thread} -- In this mode you can see which threads were executing the zone.
\item {\itshape User text} -- Splits the zones according to the custom user text (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_markingzones}{3.4}{2}3.\+4
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Zone name} -- Groups zones by the name set on a per-\/call basis (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_markingzones}{3.4}{2}3.\+4
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Call stacks} -- Zones are grouped by the originating call stack (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collectingcallstacks}{3.12}{2}3.\+12
\end{DoxyItemize}). Note that two call stacks may sometimes appear identical, even if they are not, due to an easily overlooked difference in the source line numbers.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape Parent} -- Groups zones according to the parent zone. This mode relies on the zone hierarchy and {\itshape not} on the call stack information.
\item {\itshape No grouping} -- Disables zone grouping. It may be useful when you want to see zones in order as they appear.
\end{DoxyItemize}

You may sort each group according to the {\itshape order} in which it appeared, the call {\itshape count}, the total {\itshape time} spent in the group, or the {\itshape mean time per call}. Expanding the group view will display individual occurrences of the zone, which can be sorted by application\textquotesingle{}s time, execution time, or zone\textquotesingle{}s name. Clicking the left mouse button on a zone will open the zone information window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneinfo}{5.15}{2}5.\+15). Clicking the middle mouse button on a zone will zoom the timeline view to the zone\textquotesingle{}s extent.

Clicking the left mouse button on the group name will highlight the group time data on the histogram (figure 2525). This function provides a quick insight into the impact of the originating thread or input data on the zone performance. Clicking on the {\itshape  Clear} button will reset the group selection. If the grouping mode is set to {\itshape Parent} option, clicking the middle mouse button on the parent zone group will switch the find zone view to display the selected zone.

$<$figure id="{}findzonehistogramgroup"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Zone execution time histogram with a group highlighted.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

The call stack grouping mode has a different way of listing groups. Here only one group is displayed at any time due to the need to display the call stack frames. You can switch between call stack groups by using the  and  buttons. You can select the group by clicking on the {\itshape  Select} button. You can open the call stack window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstackwindow}{5.16}{2}5.\+16) by pressing the {\itshape  Call stack} button.

Tracy displays a variety of statistical values regarding the selected function:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape mean} -- average time value,
\item {\itshape median} -- middle time value (P50),
\item {\itshape mode} -- most common time value, quantized using histogram bins,
\item {\itshape σ} -- standard deviation,
\item {\itshape coefficient of variation} -- relation of σ to mean,
\item {\itshape P75} -- 75th percentile time value,
\item {\itshape P90} -- 90th percentile time value,
\item {\itshape P99} -- 99th percentile time value,
\item {\itshape P99.\+9} -- 99.\+9th percentile time value.
\end{DoxyItemize}

The mean and median zone times are also displayed on the histogram as red (mean) and blue (median) vertical bars. Additional bars will indicate the mean group time (orange) and median group time (green). You can disable the drawing of either set of markers by clicking on the check-\/box next to the color legend.

Hovering the  mouse cursor over a zone on the timeline, which is currently selected in the find zone window, will display a pulsing vertical bar on the histogram, highlighting the bin to which the hovered zone has been assigned. In addition, it will also highlight zone entry on the zone list.

\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}
{\bfseries{Keyboard shortcut}} ~\newline
~\newline
 You may press Ctrl + F to open or focus the find zone window and set the keyboard input on the search box.
\end{DoxyRemark}
\begin{DoxyAttention}{Attention}
{\bfseries{Caveats}} ~\newline
~\newline
 When using the execution times histogram, you must know the hardware peculiarities. Read section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_checkenvironmentcpu}{2.2.2}{3}2.\+2.\+2 for more detail.
\end{DoxyAttention}
\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Delete Left icon  -\/ Caret Left icon  -\/ Caret Right icon  -\/ Check icon  -\/ Align Justify icon  -\/ Arrow Pointer icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1047}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Timeline interaction}{Timeline interaction}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1047}
The profiler will highlight matching zones on the timeline display when the zone statistics are displayed in the find zone menu. Highlight colors match the histogram display. A bright blue highlight indicates that a zone is in the optional selection range, while the yellow highlight is used for the rest of the zones.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frametimefindzone}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Frame time graph interaction}{Frame time graph interaction}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frametimefindzone}
The frame time graph (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_frametimegraph}{5.2.2}{3}5.\+2.\+2) behavior is altered when a zone is displayed in the find zone window and the {\itshape Show zone time in frames} option is selected. An accumulated zone execution time is shown instead of coloring the frame bars according to the frame time targets.

Each bar is drawn in gray color, with the white part accounting for the zone time. If the execution time is greater than the frame time (this is possible if more than one thread was executing the same zone), the overflow will be displayed using red color.

Enabling {\itshape Self time} option affects the displayed values, but {\itshape Running time} does not.

\begin{DoxyAttention}{Attention}
{\bfseries{Caveats}} ~\newline
~\newline
 The profiler might not calculate the displayed data correctly, and it may not include some zones in the reported times.
\end{DoxyAttention}
\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1048}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Limiting zone time range}{Limiting zone time range}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1048}
If the {\itshape Limit range} option is selected, the profiler will include only the zones within the specified time range (chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timeranges}{5.3}{2}5.\+3) in the data. The inclusion region will be marked with a green striped pattern. Note that a zone must be entirely inside the region to be counted. You can access more options through the {\itshape  Limits} button, which will open the time range limits window, described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timerangelimits}{5.24}{2}5.\+24.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Ruler icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1050}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Zone samples}{Zone samples}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1050}
If sampling data has been captured (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sampling}{3.18.5}{3}3.\+18.\+5), an additional expandable {\itshape  Samples} section will be displayed. This section contains only the sample data attributed to the displayed zone. Looking at this list may give you additional insight into what is happening within the zone. Refer to section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_statisticssampling}{5.6.2}{3}5.\+6.\+2 for more information about this view.

You can further narrow down the list of samples by selecting a time range on the histogram or by choosing a group in the {\itshape Found zones} section. However, do note that the random nature of sampling makes it highly unlikely that short-\/lived zones (i.\+e., left part of the histogram) will have any sample data collected.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Eye Dropper icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_compare}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Compare traces window}{Compare traces window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_compare}
Comparing the performance impact of the optimization work is not an easy thing to do. Benchmarking is often inconclusive, if even possible, in the case of interactive applications, where the benchmarked function might not have a visible impact on frame render time. Furthermore, doing isolated micro-\/benchmarks loses the application\textquotesingle{}s execution environment, in which many different parts compete for limited system resources.

Tracy solves this problem by providing a compare traces functionality, very similar to the find zone window, described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7. You can compare traces either by zone or frame timing data.

You would begin your work by recording a reference trace that represents the usual behavior of the program. Then, after the optimization of the code is completed, you record another trace, doing roughly what you did for the reference one. Finally, having the optimized trace open, you select the {\itshape  Open second trace} option in the compare traces window and load the reference trace.

Now things start to get familiar. You search for a zone, similarly like in the find zone window, choose the one you want in the {\itshape matched source locations} drop-\/down, and then you look at the histogram\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}84]\+. This time there are two overlaid graphs, one representing the current trace and the second one representing the external (reference) trace (figure 2626). You can easily see how the performance characteristics of the zone were affected by your modifications.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}84]\+:\+ When comparing frame times you are presented with a list of available frame sets, without the search box.

$<$figure id="{}comparehistogram"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Compare traces histogram.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

Note that the traces are color and symbol-\/coded. The current trace is marked by a yellow  symbol, and the external one is marked by a red  symbol.

When searching for source locations it\textquotesingle{}s not uncommon to match more than one zone (for example a search for {\ttfamily Draw} may result in {\ttfamily Draw\+Circle} and {\ttfamily Draw\+Rectangle} matches). Typically you wouldn\textquotesingle{}t want to compare execution profiles of two unrelated functions, which is prevented by the {\itshape link selection} option, which ensures that when you choose a source location in one trace, the corresponding one is also selected in the second trace. Be aware that this may still result in a mismatch, for example, if you have overloaded functions. In such a case, you will need to select the appropriate function in the other trace manually.

It may be difficult, if not impossible, to perform identical runs of a program. This means that the number of collected zones may differ in both traces, influencing the displayed results. To fix this problem, enable the {\itshape Normalize values} option, which will adjust the displayed results as if both traces had the same number of recorded zones.

\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}
{\bfseries{Trace descriptions}} ~\newline
~\newline
 Set custom trace descriptions (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_traceinfo}{5.13}{2}5.\+13) to easily differentiate the two loaded traces. If no trace description is set, the name of the profiled program will be displayed along with the capture time.
\end{DoxyRemark}
\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Folder Open icon  -\/ Lemon icon  -\/ Gem icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1053}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Source files diff}{Source files diff}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1053}
To see what changes were made in the source code between the two compared traces, select the {\itshape Source diff} compare mode. This will display a list of deleted, added, and changed files. By default, the difference is calculated from the older trace to the newer one. You can reverse this by clicking on the {\itshape Switch} button.

Please note that changes will be registered only if the file has the same name and location in both traces. Tracy does not resolve file renames or moves.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_flamegraph}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Flame graph}{Flame graph}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_flamegraph}
The flame graph is a way of showing the general performance characteristics of a program on a single chart. While the timeline view displays each zone individually, the flame graph aggregates all zones into a tree structure that better conveys where the application spends its time in relation to the program flow.

Figure 2727 shows an example flame graph. The graph shows that the program has been running for 11 seconds. Looking at the top row of the zones tree, we see that during this time one second was spent in the {\itshape Init} zone and the remaining ten seconds in the {\itshape Game loop} zone.

The rows below show the zone times of the child functions. For example, the {\itshape Game loop} zone goes into the {\itshape Logic update} and {\itshape Render} zones. Only one aggregated {\itshape Logic update} and {\itshape Render} zone is displayed, even though the {\itshape Game loop} would enter these functions hundreds of times in a 10-\/second span.

There are two different {\itshape Raycast} zones on the graph. This is because there are two code paths that lead to this function, and the graph distinguishes between them.

$<$figure id="{}flamegraphfigure"{} data-\/latex-\/placement="{}h"{}$>$

$<$figcaption$>$Flame graph.$<$/\+figcaption$>$ $<$/\+figure$>$

The default sorting order of the zones on a flame graph {\itshape approximates} the real call ordering. The program will call {\itshape Init} before entering {\itshape Game loop}, and each frame update will call {\itshape Logic update} before doing {\itshape Render}. This order is preserved. However, the logic update function may need to interleave the processing of AI entities and projectile movement\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}85]\+. This interleaving won\textquotesingle{}t be represented on the graph. Each zone will be placed in the appropriate bin in a first-\/come, first-\/served manner.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}85]\+:\+ Such design would be less than ideal, but sometimes that\textquotesingle{}s how you have to go.

You can use an alternative sorting method by enabling the {\itshape Sort by time} option. This will place the most time-\/consuming zones first (to the left) on the graph.

You can navigate the flame graph using the mouse. Use the mouse wheel to zoom in and out around the mouse pointer. Pressing the Ctrl key makes zooming more precise, while pressing the Shift key makes it faster. Dragging with the right mouse button pans the graph horizontally and vertically. The bar below the time ruler shows the current horizontal view position and can be dragged to pan the graph. The {\itshape Reset view} button resets the view to show the whole graph.

Similar to the statistics window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_statistics}{5.6}{2}5.\+6), the flame graph can operate in two modes:\+ {\itshape  Instrumentation} and {\itshape  Sampling}. In the instrumentation mode, the graph represents the zones you put in your program. In the sampling mode, the graph is constructed from the automatically captured call stack data (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sampling}{3.18.5}{3}3.\+18.\+5).

In the sampling mode, external frames from system libraries are hidden by default. These typically include internal implementation details of starting threads, handling smart pointers, and other such things that are quick to execute and not really interesting. Enabling the {\itshape  External} option will show these frames. One exception is {\itshape external tails}, or calls that your code makes that do not eventually land in your application down the call chain. Think of functions that write to a file or send data on the network. These can be time-\/consuming, and you may want to see them. There is a separate option to disable these.

The flame graph can be restricted to a specific time extent using the {\itshape Limit range} option (chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timeranges}{5.3}{2}5.\+3). You can access more options through the {\itshape  Limits} button, which will open the time range limits window, described in section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timerangelimits}{5.24}{2}5.\+24.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Syringe icon  -\/ Eye Dropper icon  -\/ Shield Halved icon  -\/ Ruler icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memorywindow}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Memory window}{Memory window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memorywindow}
You can view the data gathered by profiling memory usage (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memoryprofiling}{3.9}{2}3.\+9) in the memory window. If the profiler tracked more than one memory pool during the capture, you would be able to select which collection you want to look at, using the {\itshape  Memory pool} selection box.

The top row contains statistics, such as {\itshape total allocations} count, number of {\itshape active allocations}, current {\itshape memory usage} and process {\itshape memory span}\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}86]\+.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}86]\+:\+ Memory span describes the address space consumed by the program. It is calculated as a difference between the maximum and minimum observed in-\/use memory address.

The lists of captured memory allocations are displayed in a common multi-\/column format through the profiler. The first column specifies the memory address of an allocation or an address and an offset if the address is not at the start of the allocation. Clicking the left mouse button on an address will open the memory allocation information window\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}87]\+ (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memallocinfo}{5.12}{2}5.\+12). Clicking the middle mouse button on an address will zoom the timeline view to memory allocation\textquotesingle{}s range. The next column contains the allocation size.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}87]\+:\+ While the allocation information window is opened, the address will be highlighted on the list.

The allocation\textquotesingle{}s timing data is contained in two columns:\+ {\itshape appeared at} and {\itshape duration}. Clicking the left mouse button on the first one will center the timeline view at the beginning of allocation, and likewise, clicking on the second one will center the timeline view at the end of allocation. Note that allocations that have not yet been freed will have their duration displayed in green color.

The memory event location in the code is displayed in the last four columns. The {\itshape thread} column contains the thread where the allocation was made and freed (if applicable), or an {\itshape alloc /\+ free} pair of the threads if it was allocated in one thread and freed in another. The {\itshape zone alloc} contains the zone in which the allocation was performed\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}88]\+, or {\ttfamily -\/} if there was no active zone in the given thread at the time of allocation. Clicking the left mouse button on the zone name will open the zone information window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneinfo}{5.15}{2}5.\+15). Similarly, the {\itshape zone free} column displays the zone which freed the allocation, which may be colored yellow, if it is the same zone that did the allocation. Alternatively, if the zone has not yet been freed, a green {\itshape active} text is displayed. The last column contains the {\itshape alloc} and {\itshape free} call stack buttons, or their placeholders, if no call stack is available (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collectingcallstacks}{3.12}{2}3.\+12 for more information). Clicking on either of the buttons will open the call stack window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstackwindow}{5.16}{2}5.\+16). Note that the call stack buttons that match the information window will be highlighted.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}88]\+:\+ The actual allocation is typically a couple functions deeper in the call stack.

The memory window is split into the following sections:\+

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Box Archive icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1056}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Allocations}{Allocations}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1056}
The {\itshape @ Allocations} pane allows you to search for the specified address usage during the whole lifetime of the program. All recorded memory allocations that match the query will be displayed on a list.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1057}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Active allocations}{Active allocations}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1057}
The {\itshape  Active allocations} pane displays a list of currently active memory allocations and their total memory usage. Here, you can see where your program allocated memory it is now using. If the application has already exited, this becomes a list of leaked memory.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Heart Pulse icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1059}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Memory map}{Memory map}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1059}
On the {\itshape  Memory map} pane, you can see the graphical representation of your program\textquotesingle{}s address space. Active allocations are displayed as green lines, while the freed memory is red. The brightness of the color indicates how much time has passed since the last memory event at the given location -- the most recent events are the most vibrant.

This view may help assess the general memory behavior of the application or in debugging the problems resulting from address space fragmentation.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Map icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstacktree}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Bottom-\/up call stack tree}{Bottom-\/up call stack tree}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstacktree}
The {\itshape  Bottom-\/up call stack tree} pane is only available, if the memory events were collecting the call stack data (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collectingcallstacks}{3.12}{2}3.\+12). In this view, you are presented with a tree of memory allocations, starting at the call stack entry point and going up to the allocation\textquotesingle{}s pinpointed place. Each tree level is sorted according to the number of bytes allocated in the given branch.

Each tree node consists of the function name, the source file location, and the memory allocation data. The memory allocation data is either yellow {\itshape inclusive} events count (allocations performed by children) or the cyan {\itshape exclusive} events count (allocations that took place in the node)\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}89]\+. Two values are counted:\+ total memory size and number of allocations.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}89]\+:\+ Due to the way call stacks work, there is no possibility for an entry to have both inclusive and exclusive counts, in an adequately instrumented program.

See chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_stackwindows}{5.18}{2}5.\+18 for description of the {\itshape  Group by function name} option.

Enabling the {\itshape Only active allocations} option will limit the call stack tree only to display active allocations. Enabling {\itshape Only inactive allocations} option will have similar effect for inactive allocations. Both are mutually exclusive, enabling one disables the other. Displaying inactive allocations, when combined with {\itshape Limit range}, will show short lived allocations highlighting potentially unwanted behavior in the code.

Clicking the right mouse button on the function name will open the allocations list window (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_alloclist}{5.11}{2}5.\+11), which lists all the allocations included at the current call stack tree level. Likewise, clicking the right mouse button on the source file location will open the source file view window (if applicable, see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sourceview}{5.17}{2}5.\+17).

Some function names may be too long to correctly display, with the events count data at the end. In such cases, you may press the {\itshape control} button, which will display the events count tooltip.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Tree icon  -\/ Arrow Up icon  -\/ Layer Group icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1062}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Top-\/down call stack tree}{Top-\/down call stack tree}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1062}
The {\itshape  Top-\/down call stack tree} pane is identical in functionality to the {\itshape Bottom-\/up call stack tree}, but the call stack order is reversed when the tree is built. This means that the tree starts at the memory allocation functions and goes down to the call stack entry point.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Tree icon  -\/ Arrow Down icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1064}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Looking back at the memory history}{Looking back at the memory history}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_autotoc_md1064}
By default, the memory window displays the memory data at the current point of program execution. It is, however, possible to view the historical data by enabling the {\itshape  Limits} option. The profiler will consider only the memory events within the time range in the displayed results. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timerangelimits}{5.24}{2}5.\+24 for more information.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Ruler icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_alloclist}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Allocations list window}{Allocations list window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_alloclist}
This window displays the list of allocations included at the selected call stack tree level (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memorywindow}{5.10}{2}5.\+10 and \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstacktree}{5.10.4}{3}5.\+10.\+4).\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memallocinfo}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Memory allocation information window}{Memory allocation information window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memallocinfo}
The information about the selected memory allocation is displayed in this window. It lists the allocation\textquotesingle{}s address and size, along with the time, thread, and zone data of the allocation and free events. Clicking the {\itshape  Zoom to allocation} button will zoom the timeline view to the allocation\textquotesingle{}s extent.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Microscope icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_traceinfo}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Trace information window}{Trace information window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_traceinfo}
This window contains information about the current trace:\+ captured program name, time of the capture, profiler version which performed the capture.

There\textquotesingle{}s an text entry field for an optional custom description of the trace for you to fill in. This description will appear on the profiler window title bar, or when comparing two traces (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_compare}{5.8}{2}5.\+8), enabling you to quickly recognize what the trace contains. For some people it\textquotesingle{}s fine to just have {\itshape any} semi-\/unique description to be able to identify a specific trace. For such purposes there\textquotesingle{}s an {\itshape  Generate name} button, which will set the trace description to an abstract meaningless identifier.

If the {\itshape  Public sidecar} option is selected, the file containing trace-\/specific user settings (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_tracespecific}{9.2}{2}9.\+2) will be saved on disk next to the trace file.

Open the {\itshape Trace statistics} section to see information about the trace, such as achieved timer resolution, number of captured zones, lock events, plot data points, memory allocations, etc.

If {\itshape CPU topology} data is available (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_cputopology}{3.18.4}{3}3.\+18.\+4), you will be able to view the package, core, and thread hierarchy.

The {\itshape Source location substitutions} section allows adapting the source file paths, as captured by the profiler, to the actual on-\/disk locations\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}90]\+. You can create a new substitution by clicking the {\itshape Add new substitution} button. This will add a new entry, with input fields for ECMAScript-\/conforming regular expression pattern and its corresponding replacement string. You can quickly test the outcome of substitutions in the {\itshape example source location} input field, which will be transformed and displayed below, as {\itshape result}.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}90]\+:\+ This does not affect source files cached during the profiling run.

\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}
{\bfseries{Quick example}} ~\newline
~\newline
 Let\textquotesingle{}s say we have an Unix-\/based operating system with program sources in {\ttfamily /\+home/\+user/\+program/\+src/\+} directory. We have also performed a capture of an application running under Windows, with sources in {\ttfamily C:\+\textbackslash{}Users\textbackslash{}user\textbackslash{}Desktop\textbackslash{}program\textbackslash{}src} directory. The source locations don\textquotesingle{}t match, and the profiler can\textquotesingle{}t access the source files on our disk. We can fix that by adding two substitution patterns:\+ ~\newline
~\newline

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}C:\+\textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}Users\textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}user\textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}Desktop} {\ttfamily /\+home/\+user} ~\newline
~\newline

\item {\ttfamily \textbackslash{}\textbackslash{}} {\ttfamily /\+}
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyRemark}
By default, all source file modification times need to be older than the capture time of the trace. This can be disabled using the {\itshape Enforce source file modification time older than trace capture time} check box, i.\+e. when the source files are under source control and the file modification time is not relevant.

In this window, you can view the information about the machine on which the profiled application was running. This includes the operating system, used compiler, CPU name, total available RAM, etc. In addition, if application information was provided (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_appinfo}{3.8.1}{3}3.\+8.\+1), it will also be displayed here.

If an application should crash during profiling (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_crashhandling}{2.5}{2}2.\+5), the profiler will display the crash information in this window. It provides you information about the thread that has crashed, the crash reason, and the crash call stack (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstackwindow}{5.16}{2}5.\+16).

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


 -\/ Dice icon  -\/ User Gear icon\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_framestatistics}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Frame statistics window}{Frame statistics window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_framestatistics}
This windows shows statistical information about the selected frame set timing, and a histogram. See section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7 for a description of the displayed data. As a convenience, you can switch the active frame set here.

You can restrict the displayed frame statistics to the frame range currently visible on the screen with the {\itshape Limit to view} option, while the {\itshape Limit range} switch limits the active range to a preset time limit, as described in chapter \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_timerangelimits}{5.24}{2}5.\+24. If both limit options are active, the resulting frame range is the intersection of both ranges.\hypertarget{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneinfo}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Zone information window}{Zone information window}}\label{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_zoneinfo}
The zone information window displays detailed information about a single zone. There can be only one zone information window open at any time. While the window is open, the profiler will highlight the zone on the timeline view with a green outline. The following data is presented:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Basic source location information:\+ function name, source file location, and the thread name.
\item \doxylink{struct_timing}{Timing} information.
\item If the profiler performed context switch capture (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_contextswitches}{3.18.3}{3}3.\+18.\+3
\end{DoxyItemize}) and a thread was suspended during zone execution, a list of wait regions will be displayed, with complete information about the timing, CPU migrations, and wait reasons. If CPU topology data is available (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_cputopology}{3.18.4}{3}3.\+18.\+4), the profiler will mark zone migrations across cores with "{}\+C"{} and migrations across packages -- with "{}\+P."{} In some cases, context switch data might be incomplete\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}91]\+, in which case a warning message will be displayed.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Memory events list, both summarized and a list of individual allocation/\+free events (see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_memorywindow}{5.10}{2}5.\+10
\end{DoxyItemize}for more information on the memory events list).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item List of messages that the profiler logged in the zone\textquotesingle{}s scope. If the {\itshape exclude children} option is disabled, messages emitted in child zones will also be included.
\item Parent zones list, showing the hierarchy of parent zones that contain the current zone. Hovering the  mouse pointer over a parent zone will highlight it on the timeline view with a red outline. Clicking the left mouse button on a zone will switch the zone info window to that zone. Clicking the middle mouse button on a zone will zoom the timeline view to the zone\textquotesingle{}s extent. Clicking the right mouse button on a source file location will open the source file view window (if applicable, see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sourceview}{5.17}{2}5.\+17
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Zone call stack. It can be also displayed in a separate window with the {\itshape  Call stack} button.
\item Child zones list, showing how the current zone\textquotesingle{}s execution time was used. Zones on this list can be grouped according to their source location. Each group can be expanded to show individual entries. All the controls from the parent zones list are also available here.
\item Time distribution in child zones, which expands the information provided in the child zones list by processing {\itshape all} zone children (including multiple levels of grandchildren). This results in a statistical list of zones that were really doing the work in the current zone\textquotesingle{}s time span. If a group of zones is selected on this list, the find zone window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7
\end{DoxyItemize}) will open, with a time range limited to show only the children of the current zone.

\+[\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}91]\+:\+ For example, when capture is ongoing and context switch information has not yet been received.

\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}
{\bfseries{Call stack reconstruction}} ~\newline
~\newline
 When a zone was not instrumented with call stack capture, Tracy will still try to provide the call stack reconstruction. Note that for this to work, call stack sampling must be enabled (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sampling}{3.18.5}{3}3.\+18.\+5), and at least one sample must be captured in the zone time extent. The heuristic analysis is not perfect, and the result may be incorrect. ~\newline
~\newline
 Reconstructed call stacks are indicated with the  magic wand icon.
\end{DoxyRemark}
The zone information window has the following controls available:\+


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Zoom to zone} -- Zooms the timeline view to the zone\textquotesingle{}s extent.
\item {\itshape  Go to parent} -- Switches the zone information window to display current zone\textquotesingle{}s parent zone (if available).
\item {\itshape  Statistics} -- Displays the zone general performance characteristics in the find zone window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_findzone}{5.7}{2}5.\+7
\end{DoxyItemize}).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Call stack} -- Views the current zone\textquotesingle{}s call stack in the call stack window (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_callstackwindow}{5.16}{2}5.\+16
\end{DoxyItemize}). The button will be highlighted if the call stack window shows the zone\textquotesingle{}s call stack. Only available if zone had captured call stack data (section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_collectingcallstacks}{3.12}{2}3.\+12).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Source} -- Display source file view window with the zone source code (only available if applicable, see section \doxysectlink{md__mono_engine_2thirdparty_2tracy_2manual_2tracy_sourceview}{5.17}{2}5.\+17
\end{DoxyItemize}). The button will be highlighted if the source file is displayed (but the focused source line might be different).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\itshape  Go back} -- Returns to the previously viewed zone. The viewing history is lost when the zone information window is closed or when the type of displayed zone changes (from CPU to GPU or vice versa).
\end{DoxyItemize}

Clicking on the {\itshape  Copy to clipboard} buttons will copy the appropriate data to the clipboard.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}
